Phillips Petroleum Co. v. County of Lake


No. A051302


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


15 Cal. App. 4th 180; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 765; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 470; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3087; 93 Daily Journal DAR 5351



April 27, 1993, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * ]


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, Rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II, III, IV, V, VI, VIII and IX.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Lake County, No. 20285, Stephen R. McNelis, Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Justice Court for the former Biggs-Gridley Judicial District sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The October 3, 1990, judgment awarding Phillips a tax refund in the amount of $ 3,611,569.88, and $ 1,393,534.21 in interest, and $ 3,137.08 in costs is affirmed. Additionally, the December 6, 1991, order fixing the amount of prejudgment interest, denying Phillips's request for attorney fees, and allowing costs, is affirmed. Phillips is further entitled to postjudgment interest at the yearly rate of 7 percent per annum to be measured from October 3, 1990, the date of entry of judgment. Phillips is awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Lake County (California), which awarded plaintiff petroleum company a tax refund and interest. Plaintiff appealed a postjudgment order that denied plaintiff's request for attorney fees and fixed prejudgment interest.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff petroleum company sought a tax refund of certain property taxes assessed against its geothermal interests during seven tax years. Plaintiff contended that defendant county's method of assessment was in violation of Cal. Const. art. XIII A. The trial court agreed and awarded plaintiff a tax refund, interest, and costs. Defendant appealed the judgment. Plaintiff appealed a postjudgment order that denied its motion for attorney fees and fixed prejudgment interest. The appellate court affirmed both the judgment and the order. The court held that because geothermal interests and oil and gas interest were substantially similar, Cal. Code Regs., tit. 18, § 468, a regulation that established valuation principles for the taxation of oil and gas interests, applied to geothermal interests. The court held that under § 468, defendant should have assigned the interests a base year value as of the lien date following acquisition by plaintiff's predecessor. The court further held that an award of attorney fees was not appropriate because defendant's failure to apply § 468 was a misunderstanding of the law rather than a challenge to the validity of the provision itself.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed a judgment that awarded plaintiff petroleum company a tax refund and interest. The court found that plaintiff was entitled to the refund because defendant county misapplied the law in assessing the tax. The court also affirmed a postjudgment order that denied plaintiff's request for attorney fees and fixed prejudgment interest.

 

1028 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Bayscene Resident Negotiators v. Bayscene Mobilehome Park


No. D014430


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


15 Cal. App. 4th 119; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 626; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 444; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3049; 93 Daily Journal DAR 5194



April 23, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 631284, Lawrence Kapiloff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident negotiators sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which dismissed their petition to correct and confirm an arbitration award against respondent mobile home park owners, because the city ordinance mandating binding arbitration of mobile home rent disputes was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After respondent mobile home park owners announced a rent increase, they entered into negotiations with appellant resident negotiators pursuant to the city's ordinances providing for non-binding mediation of disputed rent-increases. While mediation was pending, the city amended its ordinance to require binding arbitration. Respondents signed an agreement to arbitrate. The arbitrator found for appellants, who then petitioned the trial court to confirm the award. The trial court dismissed the petition because it found that the city's ordinance was unconstitutional. Upon review, the court affirmed, finding that respondents did not consent to arbitration as they were threatened with criminal prosecution by the city's attorney for failure to comply with the ordinance if they did not sign the agreement. The court found that the ordinance deprived respondents of property without due process of law in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, §7(a) because the ordinance made an award final and failed to provide for judicial review in the event a party rejected an arbitration award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant resident negotiators' petition to confirm the arbitration award as the city ordinance mandating binding arbitration violated respondent mobile home park owners' due process rights. The court held that the ordinance made an award final and failed to provide for judicial review in the event that a party rejected the award.

 

1029 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Barrera


No. F017322


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


14 Cal. App. 4th 1555; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 395; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 397; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2778; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4763



April 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 23, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 467. Review Denied July 15, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3782.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 446664-5, A. Dennis Caeton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed. The judgment insofar as it relates to sentencing is vacated, and the matter is remanded for resentencing in accordance with the views expressed herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a conviction for torture, Cal. Penal Code § 206, in Superior Court of Fresno County (Calif.), on the grounds that the statute was vague and overbroad, and violated equal protection guarantees of the state, and federal constitutions, that prosecutions could not be brought because other statutes cover the same conduct it prohibits, and the trial court failed to state reasons when sentencing on a gun use enhancement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried on an information alleging torture, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 206. The jury found him guilty, and found true a gun use enhancement under § 12022.5. Appellant was sentenced to an indeterminate term of 15 years to life on the torture charge and the upper term on the gun enhancement. Appellant sought review of the conviction for § 206, on the grounds that the statute was vague and overbroad, and violated equal protection guarantees of the state and federal constitutions, that prosecutions could not be brought because other statutes cover the same conduct it prohibits, and the trial court failed to state reasons when sentencing on the gun use enhancement. The court affirmed the conviction, found that the § 206 was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad; that its application did not deny the appellant equal protection; and that it did not overlap with other statutes. The trial court did fail to state its reasons for its enhancement choice on the record as required by § 12022.5(a) The judgment insofar as it related to sentencing was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing with articulation of the factors for the enhancement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's torture conviction. The judgment insofar as it related to sentencing was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing with articulation of the factors for the enhancement, if any.

 

1030 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Greenwood Addition Homeowners Assn. v. City of San Marino


No. B069545


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


14 Cal. App. 4th 1360; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 350; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 381; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2671; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4567



April 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 1, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3606.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC 050600, Stephen E. O'Neil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, and the superior court is directed to enter judgment denying the petition for mandate. The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants city, its individual city council members, and city planning commission challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found that Cal. Gov't. Code § 99(b) required them to hear and determine plaintiffs homeowners association and members' annexation application.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs homeowners association and its members filed an application to annex their neighborhood to an adjoining city with the local planning commission. The city council terminated plaintiffs' tax transfer negotiations with Los Angeles County in connection with their petitions for annexation because of insufficient service revenue expectations. Plaintiffs filed a lawsuit against defendants city, its individual city council members, and city planning commission, and the trial court directed a writ requiring defendants city and planning commission to recommence the annexation process. On review, that court found that although Cal. Gov't. Code § 99(b) contemplated that the city and county affected by an annexation application would reach and adopt an agreement as to property tax revenues to be exchanged in the event the annexation became effective, the statute did not require the parties to do so. The trial court therefore erred in mandating defendant city to adopt such an agreement with the county regarding plaintiffs' application. The judgment was reversed, and the superior court was directed to enter judgment denying the petition for mandate.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision that required defendants city, its individual city council members, and city planning commission to hear and determine plaintiffs homeowners association and members' annexation application was reversed because the relevant statute did not require defendants to reach an agreement regarding annexation. Therefore, the trial court erred when it mandated defendants to adopt an agreement regarding plaintiffs' application.

 

1031 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



State Comp. Ins. Fund v. State Bd. of Equalization


No A058211


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE.


14 Cal. App. 4th 1295; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 526; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 377; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2644; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4519



April 9, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 10, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3148.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 927060, Lucy Kelly McCabe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance fund challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which dismissed an action for a tax refund in which appellant challenged the validity of a provision of Proposition 103 that raised the rate of the insurance premium tax. Appellant contended that the provision, codified as Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 12202.1, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurance fund challenged a judgment that dismissed an action for a tax refund in which appellant challenged the validity of a provision of Proposition 103, which raised the rate of the insurance premium tax imposed by Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 28. After paying the tax at issue, codified as Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 12202.1, appellant filed a complaint for a refund against appellee State Board of Equalization. The trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss. Appellant argued that Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 28, mandated that the legislature was authorized to change the tax rate and that appellee was directed to assess the tax at the rate the legislature decided upon. Appellant therefore argued that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 12202.1 was constitutionally invalid. The appellate court disagreed and affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant's action. The court concluded that the electorate also had the power to change the tax rate by initiative because the constitutional grant of power to the legislature in Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 28 (i), entailed a similar grant of power to the electorate to legislate through the initiative process.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing appellant insurance fund's action was affirmed because, apart from procedural differences, the electorate's lawmaking powers were identical to that of the legislature. The court held that the electorate's reserved power of statutory initiative also extended to tax legislation.

 

1032 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Avina


No A056572


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE.


14 Cal. App. 4th 1303; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 511; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 379; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2664; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4522



April 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Lake County, No. CR3357, Robert L. Crone, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the superior court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Lake County (California) convicting him of one count of continuous sexual abuse of a child, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288.5. Defendant contended he was deprived of his right to a unanimous jury verdict by an instruction, derived from language in the statute, allowing conviction without jury unanimity on which individual acts of abuse occurred.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted by a jury of one count of continuous sexual abuse of a child, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288.5. On appeal, defendant contended he was deprived of his right to a unanimous jury verdict by an instruction, derived from language in the statute, allowing conviction without jury unanimity on which individual acts of abuse occurred. The appeals court affirmed the conviction because the legislature did not deprive defendant of due process by defining in § 288.5 a course of criminal conduct crime. The court reasoned that in a prosecution for a course-of-conduct offense, where the evidence shows only a single course of conduct, the jury need not be instructed on a need for unanimity as to the conduct supporting the conviction. The court noted that § 288.5 allowed prosecutors to seek significant penalties against the resident molester, without demanding unrealistic precision from a child witness. At the same time, it limited the offender's potential liability to a single count against a given victim, thus eliminating the potential for arbitrary variation in charging and punishment present under Cal. Penal Code § 288.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed defendant's conviction for continuous sexual abuse of a child. The court ruled that because the criminal statute punished a course of conduct, the entire course of conduct constituted only one violation of the statute, and hence unanimity on each individual act was not required.

 

1033 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



County of Orange v. Leslie B.


No. G012153


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


14 Cal. App. 4th 976; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 797; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 352; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2556; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4329



March 30, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Orange County, No. AD52409, Donald E. Smallwood, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which named defendant father a child's natural and legal father. Defendant father argued that the trial court erred by refusing to presume that the mother's husband, defendant husband, was the child's father, Cal. Evid. Code § 621.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county filed a complaint against defendant husband and father to establish paternity of a 12-year old child. Defendant husband was married to the child's mother when the child was conceived, but they later divorced. Defendant father had a sexual relationship with the mother at that time. Defendant father's complaint added defendant husband as a defendant. Blood tests established that defendant father was the natural father. Defendant father appealed the order of paternity finding him to be the natural and legal father, arguing that the trial court erred by refusing to apply the presumption that defendant husband was the father, Cal. Evid. Code § 621. The court affirmed, holding that the presumption did not apply because to allow defendant father to use the statute to protect him from assuming responsibility for the child would defeat the statute's purpose, that failure to apply the statutory presumption would not disrupt any marital union because the child, the mother, and defendant husband never lived together, that declaring defendant father to be the father was in the child's best interests, and that decisions under § 621 required balancing private and state interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which held that defendant father was the natural and legal father of a child. The court held that the statutory presumption that the mother's husband, defendant husband, was the father did not apply, because to do so would defeat the purposes of the statute.

 

1034 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



City of Berkeley v. Cukierman


No. A055203


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


14 Cal. App. 4th 1331; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 478; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 402; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2772; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4810



March 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Ordered Published April 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 666288-8, Demetrios P. Agretelis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hotel owner sought relief from the judgment entered by the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), awarding relief to respondent city on appellant's cross-complaint that alleged that a business license tax ordinance passed by respondent violated the equal protection clause of the constitution. Respondent had filed suit to collect the taxes under the contested ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city enacted a business license tax ordinance, which required that certain businesses pay annual taxes. Respondent filed a complaint to collect unpaid business license taxes, and appellant hotel owner filed a cross-complaint for declaratory relief, alleging that the ordinance violated the equal protection clause of the constitution. The trial court entered judgment for respondent. Appellant sought relief. The court held that appellant was subject to a business license tax irrespective of the nature of the legal relationship between the provider and the guest. Appellant next argued that even if the disputed section of the ordinance applied to the hotel operation, it was invalid because it contravened the equal protection clause of the Constitution. The court held that the ordinance was enacted for rational reasons, and a mere disparity in the tax rate did not provide a legitimate reason to overturn the ordinance on equal protection grounds. The court concluded that the ordinance was constitutionally justified and that appellant's contention that the tax classification in the ordinance automatically failed was wrong; thus, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court upholding the business license tax ordinance because the business tax was enacted upon a rational basis, and a disparity in tax rates did not violate the equal protection clause of the constitution. Therefore, the ordinance was not contrary to equal protection standards.

 

1035 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Salazar v. Dawson


No. B066953


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


29 Cal. App. 4th 1043; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 665; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 316; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2226; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4300



March 25, 1993, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 22, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 437. Review Granted July 15, 1993 (S032696), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3738.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 14 Cal. App. 4th 95 and 19 Cal. App. 4th 982 and 24 Cal. App. 4th 1245.)] (See 9 Cal. 4th 836 now entitled Salazar v. Eastin)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. 87506, Edwin M. Osborne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Costs on appeal are awarded to appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which granted respondent state education officials' motion to vacate an injunction and writ of mandate that were issued against respondent pursuant to an appellate ruling that Cal. Educ. Code § 39807.5 violated the California Constitution.


OVERVIEW: After ruling in favor of appellant taxpayers that Cal. Educ. Code § 39807.5 violated both the free school guaranty and the equal protection clause of the state constitution, the court issued an injunction and writ of mandate against respondent state education officials. Thereafter, the trial court granted respondent's motion to vacate the injunction and writ in view of the subsequent state supreme court ruling that found § 39807.5 was facially valid. On review, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with instructions. The court noted that it was in fact the administration and implementation of § 39807.5 which was contested in the first case, not its existence. The court ruled that § 39807.5 fee waiver mandate was ignored by school districts, or if it was utilized it was not enforced uniformly or properly. Thus, the statute as applied violated the state constitution, and therefore the injunction and writ were still necessary and proper in the interests of justice. The court noted that respondent did not allege any changed facts and that the prior supreme court ruling did not affect the facts regarding the nature of the statute's application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that had vacated an injunction and writ of mandate and remanded the case with instructions. The court ruled that its injunction and writ were based on respondent state education officials' improper application of the relevant statute, not on its facial constitutionality. Thus, the court ruled that the injunction and writ were still necessary to enforce respondent's compliance with the statute.

 

1036 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Millan v. Restaurant Enterprises Group, Inc.


No. G012006


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


14 Cal. App. 4th 477; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 198; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 304; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2168; 1 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 517; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3759; 16 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1951



March 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 24, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 305. Review Denied May 19, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2633.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 665956, Donald E. Smallwood, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order compelling compliance with the subpoena is affirmed. The DSLE shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) compelling it to produce documents pursuant to an administrative subpoena issued by respondent state division of labor standards enforcement, arguing that respondent lacked the authority to investigate whether appellant was subject to the vacation pay requirements of Cal. Lab. Code § 227.3 and that the subpoena was too broad.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's order that appellant employer comply with an administrative subpoena issued by respondent state division of labor standards, which was investigating whether appellant was subject to the vacation pay provisions of Cal. Lab. Code § 227.3. It found that Cal. Lab. Code § 95(a) gave respondent power to enforce state labor laws, and that neither § 95(a) nor Cal. Gov't Code § 11180 required that a pending claim be assigned to appellee before it could make an investigation. The court rejected appellant's argument that the investigation was preempted by the Employee Retirement Income Security Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001 et seq.; although respondent could not regulate appellant's vacation benefits if they were paid out of a funded Voluntary Employees' Beneficiary Association Trust, as opposed to its general assets, respondent had the right to seek the documents to determine whether preemption applied or not. Finally, the court found, the subpoena was not overly broad because it sought records appellant was required to file, but not to retain, concluding that nothing in the law limited respondent to seeking only records appellant was required to retain.


OUTCOME: Finding that respondent state division of labor standards had the power to investigate whether appellant employer was subject to vested vacation pay law and that it was not necessary that respondent first be assigned a pending claim, the court affirmed the order that appellant comply with respondent's administrative subpoena. It rejected appellant's arguments that the investigation was preempted by ERISA and that the subpoena was overly broad.

 

1037 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Estes v. Rowland


No. A048296


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


14 Cal. App. 4th 508; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 901; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 288; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2112; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4098



March 23, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Marin County, No. 127247, Richard H. Breiner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified in accordance with the views expressed herein and, as modified, affirmed. Each party to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prison sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which entered an injunction limiting defendant's ability to conduct random searches of prison visitors' vehicles on prison property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant prison instituted a policy of conducting random searches of prison visitor's vehicles to stem the flow of illegal drugs into the prison. The trial court imposed various injunctive restrictions on the searches, and defendant appealed. The court held that the searches were a justifiable component of a comprehensive program to deal with the problem of contraband in the prisons. The court held that it was reasonable to limit search waits to 10 minutes with additional time for special circumstances not to exceed 30 minutes and written notice requirements were a proper way to acquire informed, voluntary consent. The court struck any restriction imposed after a drug sniffing dog alerted to the scent of contraband because U.S. Const. amend. IV imposed no time limits on searches founded on probable cause. The prison was permitted to deny visitation to a visitor found with contraband regardless of the manner in which it was packaged. The prohibition on soiling visitor's property was struck because there was no evidence of an inadequate remedy at law. The judgment was modified, and, as modified, affirmed.


OUTCOME: The injunction limiting the defendant prison's ability to conduct random searches of prison visitors' vehicles on prison property was modified in accordance with the views expressed in the opinion and, as modified, affirmed because the defendant's policy was a justifiable component of a comprehensive program to deal with the problem of contraband in the prisons.

 

1038 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


In re Bounmy V.


No. F017956.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


29 Cal. App. 4th 931; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 557; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 292; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2131; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3767



March 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 24, 1993 (S032633), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3373.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 14 Cal. App. 4th 494 and 19 Cal. App. 4th 904 and 24 Cal. App. 4th 778.)] Review Dismissed November 23, 1994 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 5th Dist. ( rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Stanislaus County, No. 24874, John E. Griffin, Jr., Judge, and Timothy J. Helfer, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, Section 21.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a minor, sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California), which denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 700.1 and found that defendant violated Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351.5 for possession of cocaine base for sale.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a minor, was found to have violated Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351.5 for possession of cocaine base for sale. Pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 725(b), defendant was adjudged a ward of the court and released on probation. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence obtained during his arrest pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 700.1 was denied. The court found that the carport where the arrest and search occurred was a public place, thereby negating defendant's arguments based on a warrantless search or arrest. As a minor, the court found that defendant was afforded full protection under U.S. Const. amend. IV. This included the requirement of probable cause for arrest, but the facts showed that the police officers had prior knowledge of suspicious activity by defendant, which established grounds for a detention and investigation, even though they did not have probable cause to arrest. The court affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress evidence and held that even though the evidence was obtained by unlawful police conduct, it would have been discovered even without the unlawful act and was an exception to the exclusionary rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence and held that while the exclusionary rule prohibited the introduction of unlawfully obtained evidence, the evidence obtained as the result of unlawful police conduct was admissible because the evidence would have been discovered even if no constitutional violation occurred.

 

1039 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People ex rel. Dept. of Transportation v. Diversified Properties Co. III


No. E009497


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


14 Cal. App. 4th 429; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 676; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 286; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2072; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3942



March 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 23, 1993. Review Denied July 1, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3616.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. RCV 46430, Philip E. Schaefer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment in condemnation entered below is reversed insofar as it: (1) Awarded DPC damages for so-called "unreasonable pre-condemnation activities" by the State; and (2) ordered interest, calculated at a 10 percent postjudgment interest rate, on the compensation awarded to DPC. In all other respects, the judgment entered below is affirmed in full.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state, ex relatione the state department of transportation, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, San Bernardino County (California), which found a de facto taking, awarded damages for unreasonable delay by the state in instituting its direct condemnation action, and imposed a 10 percent postjudgment interest rate on the compensation and damages awarded to defendant landowner.


OVERVIEW: The state, ex relatione the state department of transportation, condemned defendant landowner's property under its power of eminent domain. The trial court awarded defendant damages for the state's unreasonable delay in instituting its direct condemnation action and imposed a 10 percent postjudgment interest rate. The court affirmed the judgment in part and held that there was substantial evidence that the state effected a de facto taking prior to the filing of the eminent domain action. The court reversed the judgment that assessed damages for unreasonable pre-condemnation activities and applied a 10 percent postjudgment interest rate. The state was not liable for damages because the delay occurred after the de facto taking; there would have been a duplication in damages because defendant received full payment on its condemnation award, which ran from the date of the de facto taking. The trial court incorrectly calculated the proper interest rate; it should have independently determined the extant market rate of interest and then applied the higher of that rate or the legislatively-created apportionment rate set forth in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1268.350.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that awarded defendant landowner damages for pre-condemnation activities by the state, ex relatione the state department of transportation, and ordered postjudgment interest. The court affirmed the judgment in part and held that the state effected a de facto taking prior to the eminent domain action. The state was not liable for damages due to delay that occurred after de facto taking.

 

1040 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Long Beach Lesbian & Gay Pride, Inc. v. City of Long Beach


No. B060704


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


14 Cal. App. 4th 312; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 861; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 275; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1999; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3564



March 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 24, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3388.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 549716, Charles S. Litwin, Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Los Angeles Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed insofar as it sustains the constitutionality of section 5.60.070 with respect to parades, and of section 5.60.030 insofar as it provides for a 30-working-day permit application period for parades and for waiver thereof, and fails to provide a time limit for decision of a parade permit application. The trial court shall enter declaratory judgment for plaintiffs on those issues. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed. The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged the order of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), which held that Long Beach, Cal., Municipal Code ch. 5.60 imparted unconstitutionally broad administrative discretion over the grant or denial of parade permits, and since the section could not have been severed, the ordinance was entirely invalid. Plaintiff activists challenged the finding that the requirement that permittees carry insurance was proper.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff activists challenged the constitutionality of a parade permit ordinance, Long Beach, Cal., Municipal Code ch. 5.60. Defendant city appealed the trial court's judgment that the ordinance imparted unconstitutionally broad administrative discretion over the grant or denial of parade permits, and because the section could not be severed, the ordinance was entirely invalid. Plaintiff appealed the trial court's judgment that held constitutional the requirement that permittees pay for services and carry insurance. The court affirmed and held that Long Beach, Cal., Municipal Code § 5.60.030(C) unconstitutionally granted unrestrained discretion to grant or deny parade permits, and because the section could not be severed, the entire ordinance was unconstitutional. The court held that except for the insurance requirement and the provisions for the timing of permit applications, the other challenged aspects of ch. 5.60 were valid. The court could not discern sufficient justification for a blanket 30-day application requirement. It was not clear that the insurance requirement did not turn on the content of the parade.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in so much as it sustained the constitutionality of the ordinance, allowed a 30-working-day permit application period for parades, and allowed the absence of a time limit for decision of a parade permit application. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects. The ordinance that governed the issuance of parade permits unconstitutionally granted defendant city unrestrained discretion.

In re Alexander K.


No. A057245


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


14 Cal. App. 4th 549; 18 Cal. Rptr. 2d 22; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 346; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2438



March 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Ordered Published March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 91-00733, John C. Minney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The Department did not bear its burden of proving the subdivision (c) allegations. Accordingly, we reverse the jurisdictional order. The dispositional orders and all subsequent orders are moot. The Department's requests for judicial notice and augmentation concerning the dispositional issues are denied as also moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of orders of the Superior Court, Contra Costa County (California) that granted respondent department's petition, sustaining jurisdictional findings concerning appellant's son and that prohibited visitation and contact between appellant and his son except as agreed upon by their respective therapists.


OVERVIEW: Respondent department filed a petition alleging appellant father had molested his son on numerous occasions. The next month respondent filed an amended petition with six specific allegations. At the conclusion of a subsequent jurisdictional hearing, the trial court found, as a result of appellant's conduct, the child suffered emotional damage and was in danger of suffering additional damage, and, thus, the child came within Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 300(c). However, the trial court also found respondent failed to show the father sexually abused his son by a preponderance of the evidence. A dispositional hearing was then held, and the trial court ordered visitation to be arranged and supervised as agreed upon by therapists for the child and appellant. It also ordered a reunification plan for appellant, which included instructions directing appellant to enter weekly therapy. In response, appellant sought review, attacking both the jurisdictional and dispositional orders. On review, the court reversed the jurisdictional order, and declared the dispositional orders moot, because respondent failed to bear its burden of proving the § 300(c) allegations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the jurisdictional order, and declared all subsequent orders moot, because respondent department failed to prove the required statutory allegations, and the sustained allegations focused on the child's behavior and reactions, not appellant father's behavior.

People v. Lagunas


No. B066383.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


29 Cal. App. 4th 908; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 529; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 277; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2005; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3561



March 18, 1993, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted July 1, 1993 (S032503), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3596.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 14 Cal. App. 4th 291 and 19 Cal. App. 4th 881 and 24 Cal. App. 4th 755.)] (See 8 Cal. 4th 1030)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. PA006244, John H. Leahy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's order modifying the verdict is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which modified a jury's verdict of first degree burglary by finding defendant guilty of the lesser included offense of receiving stolen property.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of the crime of first degree burglary, a felony, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 459. Defendant brought a motion for new trial, which included, as an alternative to granting a new trial, a request to modify the verdict to the lesser charge of receiving stolen property, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 496(1). The trial court found that the verdict was contrary to evidence and may have been contrary to law. The trial court modified the verdict by finding defendant guilty of the lesser included offense of receiving stolen property. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that it had the nonstatutory authority to modify the verdict to a lesser related offense, upon a defense request for such consideration, because the evidence showed defendant to be not guilty of the crime of which he was convicted, but guilty of the lesser related crime. The court held that the right to modify a verdict to a lesser related offense on a motion for new trial was just as much an aspect of fundamental fairness required by due process as the right to a verdict or finding of a lesser related offense in a nonjury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order modifying the verdict, holding that the trial court had the nonstatutory authority to modify the verdict to the lesser related offense, upon a defense request for such consideration, because the evidence showed defendant to be not guilty of the crime of which he was convicted, but guilty of the lesser related crime.

Public Employment Relations Bd. v. Superior Court


No. C011909


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 1816; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 323; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 239; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1891; 142 L.R.R.M. 2831; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3374



March 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review of Real Parties in Interest Denied May 27, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 91-084, Joe S. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing respondent court to vacate its order denying the Board's application for enforcement of its subpoenas and to enter a new order granting the application.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public employment relations board sought a writ of mandate to respondent Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), directing respondent to enforce administrative subpoenas served upon real party in interest, department of personnel administration.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner public employment relations board issued subpoenas to real party in interest, department of personnel administration, in a proceeding to determine whether, in failing to meet and confer with state employee organizations prior to proposing statutes altering the terms of employment, the administration of the state governor committed unfair labor practices under the Ralph C. Dills Act (the act), Cal. Gov't Code §§ 3512 - 3524. Real party in interest opposed the enforcement of the subpoenas on the ground that petitioner lacked jurisdiction to proceed in the administrative action because the act did not extend to a governor's proposals for legislation. Respondent trial court denied petitioner's application to enforce the subpoena, concluding that the charges made were not a violation of the act. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate directing respondent to vacate its order and to enter a new order granting petitioner's application. The court found no clear failure to state a cause of action and, hence, no clear lack of petitioner's jurisdiction, which afforded a warrant for judicial intervention prior to a final determination by petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate directing respondent trial court to enforce administrative subpoenas served upon real party in interest, department of personnel administration, by petitioner public employment relations board. Respondent erred in failing to grant petitioner's application for enforcement of the subpoenas because there was no clear lack of petitioner's jurisdiction to make a final determination of the action.

In re Joshua H.


No. F017994, No. F018435


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 1718; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 282; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 226; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1744; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3153



March 8, 1993, Decided

* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts IIB through E, III and IV.

** Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied. The appeal from the disposition order is dismissed. The order granting a stay of the section 366.26 hearing is vacated; the stay of such hearing is dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the ruling of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California) which declined to order of reunification with her minor child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother challenged an order which denied her reunification rights with her minor child after it was discovered that the mother knew her boyfriend was abusing her son. Appellant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support the Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 300 finding that she was not fit to regain custody of her son. The court held that the record contained facts that supported the conclusion that appellant's boyfriend committed more than one act of physical abuse on the child, and there was sufficient evidence to support a finding of severe physical abuse as defined in Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 300. Given appellant's admission that she knew her boyfriend was abusing her child, the court denied appellant's writ petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court because it was shown that there was sufficient evidence to prove that appellant knew of the abuse inflicted upon her son, and therefore, she was not allowed to regain custody.

 

1045 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Joshua H.


No. H008944


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 1734; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 291; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 227; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1747



March 8, 1993, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part IIIB.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied June 24, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3412.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 95693, Thomas C. Edwards, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) that found defendant violated the state's hate crime statute Cal. Penal Code § 422.7(a), a felony. California's hate crime statute was part of the Tom Bane Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 52.1; Cal. Penal. Code §§ 422.5-422.95.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a judgment that found him guilty of violating the states' hate crime statute, Cal. Penal Code § 422.7(a), after physically attacking a gay neighbor. The court affirmed the judgment on the basis that § 422.7 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that the statute was not void for vagueness as it had been construed to require proof of a specific intent to deprive an individual of a right secured by federal or state law. The court found the statute not overly broad as it was narrowly drawn to protect a compelling state interest and did not attempt to prohibit bigotry itself, but the discriminatory act of selecting a crime victim based on his or her race or other status. The court stated the violent conduct proscribed by § 422.7 was not sufficiently imbued with elements of communication to be protected as expressive conduct and labeled "speech." The court stated that even if the hate crime statute enhanced penalties based on the perpetrator's bigoted thoughts, the statute targeted discriminatory conduct, not speech, and therefore fell within exceptions to the First Amendment prohibition of content discrimination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because California's hate crime statute was narrowly drawn to protect a compelling state interest and proscribed violent discriminatory conduct, not constitutionally protected expression.

 

1046 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


In re Rance H.


No. B064667


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


13 Cal. App. 4th 1537; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 264; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 208; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1589; 93 Daily Journal DAR 2862



March 3, 1993, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 3, 1993 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3065.
Kennard, J., is of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NJ01551, Rena Koppleman, Juvenile Court Referee, and Charles R. Scarlett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed for a new jurisdictional hearing under section 602.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a disposition made by a juvenile court referee in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that sustained the petition that charged defendant with possessing a short-barreled rifle. Defendant argued that the referee lacked jurisdiction to sustain the petition, because a written stipulation of the parties as mandated by Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 248 was not made.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile court referee conducted a jurisdictional hearing but did not obtain a stipulation pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 248. Defense counsel refused to sign it during the hearing, because the referee improperly questioned a witness for the state. The juvenile court referee denied the parties' joint motion for a mistrial and sustained the petition that charged defendant with possession of a firearm. On appeal, defendant argued that the referee lacked the fundamental power to act as a temporary judge at the jurisdictional hearing. The reviewing court reversed the trial court's decision and the case was remanded for a new hearing. The court held that the adjudications based upon the referee's purported exercise of judicial powers could not stand for lack of jurisdiction. Since § 248 unambiguously prohibited a referee from presiding over a jurisdictional hearing unless the parties entered into a written stipulation, the court concluded that the stipulation was a mandatory requisite to the authority of the referee to perform anything beyond "subordinate judicial duties." The court's decision was not based on sufficiency of the evidence, so double jeopardy did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment against defendant juvenile was reversed, because the juvenile court referee was without jurisdiction to sustain the charging petition absent the statutorily required written stipulation. Since the matter was not reversed on sufficiency of the evidence grounds, double jeopardy did not apply, and the case was remanded for a new jurisdictional hearing.

Miranda v. Superior Court


No. D017905


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE.


13 Cal. App. 4th 1628; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 858; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 213; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1690; 93 Daily Journal DAR 2985



March 3, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR134235, Norbert Ehrenfreund, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The stay issued November 20, 1992, is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision of respondent, the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that denied his pretrial motion to suppress evidence under Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5. Petitioner was charged with unlawful possession of controlled substances while armed with a loaded firearm, ex-felon in possession of a firearm, and possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought to suppress evidence obtained from a warrantless search of his residence on the basis that the search was made in violation of Const. amend. IV. Respondent trial court denied petitioner's motion. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was barred. The court ruled that the "good faith" exception to the rule of exclusion did not apply because the search was conducted without a warrant, and was based on erroneous information developed by the police department itself. The court noted that the "good faith" exception applied to searches conducted as a result of a police officer's reliance on a warrant, valid on its face, but later found to be defective for reasons beyond the control of the police department. Accordingly, the court held that evidence from the invalid warrantless search of petitioner's residence should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that petitioner's motion to suppress should have been granted. The court held that the evidence was subject to suppression because it was collected from a warrantless search based upon incorrect information from within the police department.

College Hospital, Inc. v. Superior Court


No. G012669.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


29 Cal. App. 4th 142; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 833; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 196; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1467; 93 Daily Journal DAR 2652



February 26, 1993, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 24, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 309. Review Granted May 13, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2519.
Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous Cites 13 Cal. App. 4th 1193, 18 Cal. App. 4th 1378, 23 Cal. App. 4th 1033.) (See 8 Cal. 4th 704)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 657016, Robert A. Knox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We conclude the trial court properly allowed the amendment alleging punitive damages against College Hospital. Accordingly, the alternative writ of mandate is discharged, and the hospital's petition for a writ of mandate is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital sought writ relief from respondent Superior Court of Orange County (California) which granted plaintiff injured parties' motion to amend their complaint to add a claim for punitive damages. Plaintiffs brought suit against petitioner and physician employee for professional negligence. Petitioner claimed that the evidence was insufficient to establish a substantial probability of success on the punitive damages claim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured parties moved to amend their complaint for professional negligence of a health care provider to add punitive damages claims against petitioner hospital and its physician employee. Respondent trial court found that plaintiffs' declarations and deposition testimony established "a substantial probability" that they would prevail on the claims, and respondent granted the motion. The hospital thereafter petitioned for writ relief, claiming that the evidence was insufficient to establish a substantial probability of success. The court denied the petition. The evidence submitted by plaintiffs was sufficient to make a prima facie case for the award of punitive damages. A trier of fact could find that petitioner's failure to properly investigate the relationship between plaintiff and the physician employee constituted both petitioner's ratification of the acts and malicious behavior on its own part. Such a finding would justify the imposition of punitive damages. Furthermore, a trier of fact could find that the physician employee's malicious acts should be imputed to petitioner so as to render it personally guilty of malice.


OUTCOME: Petitioner hospital's alternative writ of mandate was denied and discharged because respondent trial court properly allowed plaintiff injured parties to amend their complaint to allege punitive damages against petitioner. The evidence submitted by plaintiffs was sufficient to make a prima facie case for the award of punitive damages against petitioner.

Digital Biometrics, Inc. v. Anthony


No. C011227


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 1145; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 43; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 192; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1542; 93 Daily Journal DAR 2738



February 26, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sacramento County, Nos. CV365029 and CV365891, James Timothy Ford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied relief in a consolidated action that sought review of respondent deputy and deputy director of the state board of control's decision by administrative mandate and which sought to prevent respondents from entering into a contract with another contractor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contractor bid on a contract, and the evaluation team granted the bid to another contractor. Appellant submitted a letter of protest, and respondents, deputy and deputy director of the state board of control, held an administrative hearing that recommended that the protest be dismissed. Appellant filed a petition seeking review of the decision, and its attorney filed suit on behalf of other corporations alleging that respondents' contract with another contractor did not consider minority and women business participation goals and that there was a provision for an illegal advance payment. The trial court consolidated the actions and denied relief in both actions. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellant's added claims were untimely, that respondents had correctly determined the extent of their jurisdiction, and that both respondents and the administrative law judge had properly limited appellant's protest to the claim that its bid should have been selected pursuant to Cal. Pub. Cont. Code § 12102 (f). As for the claim filed by the other corporations, the court held that no statute permitted private parties to bring an action to declare a public contract void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied relief in a consolidated action that sought review of the decision of respondent deputy and deputy director of the state board of control. The court held that appellant contractor's additional claims regarding the consideration of women and minorities were raised in an untimely manner and that private parties were not permitted to bring an action to declare a public contract void.

 

1051 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Smith


No. E009425


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


13 Cal. App. 4th 1182; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 820; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 186; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1421; 93 Daily Journal DAR 2618



February 26, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR-35759, Robert D. Macomber, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) in a jury trial for robbery and kidnapping. His sentence was enhanced under Cal. Penal Code § 667.9 because he had a prior robbery conviction and because the current victim was a person 65 years or older, and such condition was known or reasonably should have been known to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery and kidnapping after he pushed a 67 year old woman into her car and drove away. His sentence was enhanced, in part, because the victim was over 65 years of age, and he had a prior conviction for robbery under Cal. Penal Code § 667.9. The court of appeal affirmed. The language of the statute that defendant knew or reasonably should have known that the victim was over 65 was not unconstitutionally vague. Case law upheld the "reasonable knowledge" standard for other enhancement statutes. Defendant was protected from increased sentence, if, for example, he robbed someone who looked younger than 65 but was older than 65 because the statute required that he knew or should have known of the victim's age. The evidence supported the enhancement because the victim was over 65, and her physical appearance was evidence for the jury to consider. Under the reviewing standard that the evidence would be viewed most favorable to the state, the court could not overturn the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal affirmed the conviction of defendant for robbery and kidnapping and his sentence enhancement for having a prior felony conviction and robbing a person 65 years or over. The enhancement statute was not void for vagueness because it required a finding that defendant knew or reasonably should have known the person was over 65. The verdict was sufficient because the victim was 67, and her physical appearance was evident.

Fielder v. City of Los Angeles


No. B068533


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


14 Cal. App. 4th 137; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 630; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 294; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2217; 93 Daily Journal DAR 4293

DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) granting defendant city's motion for summary judgment in an action challenging the validity of a municipal real estate transfer tax.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff homeowners were required to pay a tax to defendant city upon selling their residences. Plaintiffs filed an action against defendant, seeking a declaration that the transfer tax violated Cal. Const. art. XIII A, § 4, and that it was preempted by Cal. Gov't Code § 53725(a). The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the action. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that plaintiffs' contentions lacked merit. The court further found that the transfer tax was purely local in its effects and that it did not violate the state constitution. Finally, the court found that the transfer tax was not preempted by Cal. Gov't Code § 53725(a).


OUTCOME: The order granting defendant city's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff homeowners' action challenging the validity of a municipal real estate transfer tax was affirmed because the transfer tax did not violate the state constitution and it was not preempted by a state statute.

 

1053 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Hackler


No. F014589


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 1049; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 681; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 169; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1331



February 24, 1993, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II through V.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Tulare County, No. 28113, Howard R. Broadman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order revoking probation and the judgment of sentence are reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who was convicted of shoplifting beer, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which on its own motion arraigned appellant for violating a probation condition that required him to wear a T-shirt bearing a printed statement of his status as a felony theft probationer. Appellant contended that the probation condition was unconstitutional and not reasonably related to the goal of rehabilitation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, who was convicted of shoplifting beer, challenged a probation condition that required that he wear a T-shirt bearing a printed statement of his status as a felony theft probationer. The requirement applied whenever appellant was outside his residence. Appellant and another man were apprehended when each took two 12-packs of beer from a store without paying for them. Appellant challenged the validity of the T-shirt condition on the grounds that it was vague, overbroad, and not reasonably related to the goal of rehabilitation. The prosecution argued that appellant waived his challenge by failing to appeal from the order granting probation and by failing to assert the challenge at the probation revocation hearing. The appellate court disagreed on the ground that the lower court itself had raised the validity of the T-shirt condition at the probation revocation hearing. Rather than facilitating appellant's rehabilitation, the appellate court held that the T-shirt condition impinged on appellant's inalienable right to privacy guaranteed by Cal. Const. art. I, § 1. The court therefore reversed the order revoking appellant's probation.


OUTCOME: The order revoking appellant's probation and the judgment of sentence were reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion that the condition could adversely affect appellant's ability to carry on activities having no possible relationship to the offense for which he was convicted or to future criminality. The court therefore held that the condition was unreasonably overbroad and as such was invalid.

CHECKER MOTORS CORP. v. SUPERIOR COURT


No. B068424


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.


13 Cal. App. 4th 1007; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 618; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 179; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1391



February 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 3, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3069.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BS006912, Kurt J. Lewin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner out-of-state entities filed a petition for a writ of mandate seeking a reexamination of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied petitioners' motion to quash service of summons in an action in which real party in interest California Insurance Commissioner added petitioners to a conservation order.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner out-of-state entities solicited and negotiated an investment from a California insurance company, and in return they made the insurer the sole limited partner in the out-of-state partnership. Real party in interest California Insurance Commissioner was appointed conservator of the insurer by the superior court, which placed all of the insurer's property in the court's custody. Petitioners sent the insurer a letter terminating the partnership, filed an action in Delaware that sought a declaration that the insurer defaulted on the partnership agreement, which Delaware dismissed, and then filed an action to quash the service of summons, which the superior court denied. Petitioners then sought a writ of mandate. The court denied petitioners' writ, holding that while petitioners' contacts with California were not sufficient to confer general jurisdiction on the superior court, petitioners' efforts to solicit and negotiate with the insurer were sufficient to satisfy minimum contacts with California, which due process required. The court held that petitioners purposefully availed themselves to California benefits. Thus, California courts had jurisdiction over them.


OUTCOME: The court denied granting petitioner out-of-state entities' request for writ of mandate and affirmed the order of the superior court that denied petitioner's motion to quash service of summons. The court held that petitioners had purposefully availed themselves to the benefits of California and had established sufficient minimum contacts in its negotiations with a California insurance company to confer jurisdiction on the court.

 

1055 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Diaz


No. H010338, No. H010340


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 1755; 17 Cal. Rptr. 2d 395; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 274; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2077; 93 Daily Journal DAR 3614



February 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Ordered Published March 18, 1993.
As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 18, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 271. Review Denied June 10, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 3164.



DISPOSITION: Petitioners are not entitled to credits under section 2933 unless such credits have already been promised to them by officials of the Department of Corrections. The petitions for writs of habeas corpus are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, all of whom stood convicted of murder and were serving indeterminate life sentences under Cal. Penal Code § 190, filed petitions for writs of habeas corpus seeking one-for-one work conduct credits pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2933.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were convicted murderers who were serving indeterminate life sentences under Cal Penal Code § 190. They filed writs of habeas corpus in which they sought one-for-one work conduct credits pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2933. The court held that petitioners were not entitled to the credit that they sought. The court held that the plain meaning of Cal. Penal Code § 190 was that the statute applied to every person convicted of murder and that such persons had to be sentenced under § 190 and receive the punishment that it prescribed. That punishment was not reducible by one-for-one work time credits. The court also held that allowing one-for-one credits under Cal. Penal Code § 667.7, the recidivist statute, would violate the intent of voters who prescribed no such credits for people sentenced for murder under an initiative of which § 190 was a part.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioners writs of habeas corpus because they were not entitled to the credits that they sought. The court reasoned that appellants had to receive the punishment that the statute under which they were sentenced prescribed and that that punishment was not reducible by one-to-one work time credits.

State Bd. of Education v. Honig


No. C012467


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT,


13 Cal. App. 4th 720; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 727; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 153; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1193



February 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 27, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2957.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING; application for a writ of mandate. Writ issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Board of Education brought an application for a writ of mandate seeking to compel respondent Superintendent of Public Instruction to implement a series of its adopted policies as to program guidelines, budget, and administrative appointments, in a test of the division of powers under Cal. Const. art. IX, § 2.1.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute of their respective authority under Cal. Const. art. IX, § 2.1, petitioner State Board of Education sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent Superintendent of Public Instruction to implement its policies on program guidelines, appointment of superintendents and staff, budget approval, and to process a legal services contract for the litigation. The court granted a writ of mandate requiring respondent to submit nominations for superintendents, and implement petitioner's request for additional staff and for the review of employee performance evaluations, and process petitioner's legal services contract. The court rejected the remaining requests as moot or unripe. The court held that under Cal. Sch. Code § 2.1321 (1929), and Cal. Educ. Code § 3330, petitioner had the duty to determine, and respondent the duty to execute, policy, and their relationship was similar to the relationship of a corporate board of directors and its chief executive officer.


OUTCOME: Petitioner State Board of Education was granted a writ of mandate directing respondent Superintendent of Public Instruction to implement specific education policies, and process petitioner's legal services contract, because petitioner had constitutional and statutory authority to set policy, and respondent had the duty to implement it.

People v. Ward


No. E008949


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


18 Cal. App. 4th 1339; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 864; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 141; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1127



February 17, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted May 13, 1993 (S031972), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2524.
Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous Cite 13 Cal. App. 4th 630.) October 14, 1993 Review Dismissed and Remanded to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Appellate District, Division One, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 5404.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR-35266, Ronald R. Heumann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The findings as to the prior convictions are reversed as to both defendants. The cause is remanded to the trial court with directions to resentence defendants after a new trial on the issue of the prior convictions. The order denying defendants' new trial motions is also reversed and remanded with directions to the trial court to reconsider the motions under the appropriate standard.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, convicted of robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211 and falsely representing identity to a police officer in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 148.9, subd. (a), appealed their convictions from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, convicted of robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211 and falsely representing identity to a police officer in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 148.9, subd. (a), appealed their sentences. Defendants received enhanced punishments under Cal. Penal Code § 667.9, for a victim over the age of sixty-five, Cal. Penal Code § 667, for a prior offense, and Cal. Penal Code § 667.5(b), for a felony committed within five years of completing a prison term. Defendants' counsel told the trial court that they would waive their right to a jury trial on the prior conviction allegations, but the defendants never expressly waived their right to a jury trial. The court reversed the trial court's findings on the prior convictions because as with a charged offense, waiver of a jury trial on the issue of a prior conviction could not be implied. The case was remanded for resentencing; the prior conviction allegations did not implicate double jeopardy and hence there was no bar to retrial of that issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for resentencing because defendants did not waive their right to a jury trial on the prior conviction allegations. The resentencing would not violate double jeopardy because defendants were being punished only for their current conviction.

Professional Engineers v. Department of Transportation


No. A057897


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


13 Cal. App. 4th 585; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 599; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 138



February 17, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 13, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2550.
Mosk, J., Panelli, J., and Kennard, J., are of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 933930, Stuart R. Pollak, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, engineering labor organization and taxpayers, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court for the City and County of San Francisco (California), which found in favor of respondent California Department of Transportation in appellants' action contesting respondent's authority to enter into public transportation projects. Respondent entered into these agreements pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 143.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 143, respondent California Department of Transportation entered into contracts with four entities for the construction of four public transportation demonstration projects. Appellants, engineering labor organization and taxpayers, sought extraordinary, injunctive, and declarative relief, challenging respondent's authority to enter into these agreements. The trial court entered judgment denying appellants all requested relief. On appeal, the court held that the agreements did not expressly bargain away the state's police power; rather the reservation of this power was implicit in the agreements. The civil service provisions of Cal. Const. art. VII, did not preclude respondent from entering into agreements with private firms for provision of public transportation. The court held that §143, did not prohibit respondent from committing to airspace leases for commercial improvements to facilitate the projects. The court held that Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 143(d), permitted more than one facility per project and that the 35-year lease limitation applied to each facility and not the franchise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied relief to appellants, engineering labor organization and taxpayers, in their action challenging respondent California Department of Transportation's authority to enter into contracts with private entities for the construction of public transportation demonstration projects. The contracts did not abrogate the potential future exercise of the state's sovereign police power.

Wachs v. Curry


No. B064040


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.
