OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for defendants, Commissioner of Labor and other officials', because the Talent Agency Act was constitutional and enforceable aginst plaintiffs and defendants provided a sufficient rational basis for the exemption.

Marin Independent Journal v. Municipal Court


No. A058902


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE.


12 Cal. App. 4th 1712; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 550; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 120; 21 Media L. Rep. 1052; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 981; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1865



February 8, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal Court for the Marin Judicial District of Marin County, John Stephen Graham, Judge, and Albert C. Wollenberg, Jr., Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the San Francisco Municipal Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The order to show cause is discharged, and the petition for writ of mandate is denied. Respondent municipal court shall continue in possession of the film, per our previous order, and shall destroy the film


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for writ of mandate seeking relief from an order of the Municipal Court for the Marin Judicial District of Marin County (California), which denied petitioner's motion for return of a roll of film confiscated from one of its photographers who took photographs in a court proceeding on violation of Cal. R. Ct. 980.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a motion for return of a roll of film that contained photographs taken at a court proceeding in violation of the judge's order pursuant to Cal. R. Ct. 980. The lower court denied the motion. Petitioner filed a writ of mandate seeking relief from the order and alleged that the confiscation was an unconstitutional prior restraint of free speech in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. On review the court denied the writ of mandate. The court held that pursuant to Cal. R. Ct. 980, the lower court had the authority to ban court photography completely. Therefore, the seizure of the film did not give rise to a restraint of free speech, but rather, enforced the lower court order that prohibited the photographs during the court proceeding. The court opined that the seizure was not analogous to a prior restraint on free speech because the contents of the roll of film seized were not obtained lawfully. The contents were obtained in a knowing and deliberate violation of the law. Thus, the writ of mandate was refused and the lower court was ordered to maintain possession of the film and to destroy it upon final resolution of the matter.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's writ of mandate was denied, because the lower court's refusal to return a confiscated roll of film that contained photographs obtained in violation of a court order was not an unconstitutional prior restraint of free speech.

Planned Parenthood Shasta-Diablo Inc. v. Williams


No. A055117.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


23 Cal. App. 4th 532; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 540; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 111; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 957; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1776



February 5, 1993, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 225. Review Granted May 13, 1993 (S031593), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2522.
Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 12 Cal. App. 4th 1817 and 18 Cal. App. 4th 359.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Solano County, No. 110090, Dennis W. Bunting, Judge.



DISPOSITION: To summarize, we strike paragraph 4 of the permanent injunction as an unconstitutional restriction on the content of appellants' speech. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, anti-abortion protesters, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Solano County (California), which granted a permanent injunction against them in respondent abortion clinic's suit against them.


OVERVIEW: In respondent abortion clinic's suit against appellants, anti-abortion protesters, the trial court granted a permanent injunction against appellants. On appeal, the court affirmed, but struck a provision prohibiting speech in front of children. The court held that respondent had standing to bring suit to exclude appellants from its parking lot because they had a "possessory interest" in the parking lot, and appellants' activities were aimed at disrupting and impeding its lawful business. The court held that the provisions excluding appellants from the clinic parking lot and from the public sidewalk directly in front of the clinic did not violate Cal. Const. art. I, § 2 or Cal. Const. art. I, § 1. The parking lot was not a public forum, the injunction was content neutral, was narrowly tailored to serve significant government interests of keeping the free flow of vehicle and pedestrian traffic, and a woman's right to privacy, and left open ample alternative means of communication. The court held that the restrictions as to speech in front of children was unconstitutional because it limited "core political speech" and did not serve a compelling governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an injunction against appellant anti-abortion protesters, in respondent abortion clinic's suit, but struck a portion as an unconstitutional restriction on the content of appellants' speech. Place restrictions were proper as the parking lot was not a public forum, government interests were served, and there were ample alternative means of communication. Content restrictions limited "core political speech."

Johnson v. State Bar


No. B064779


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


12 Cal. App. 4th 1561; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 6; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 101; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 831; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1560



February 5, 1993, Decided


NOTICE:   [***1] Ordered Published February 2, 1993.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied April 15, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2091.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BS010877, Ronald M. Sohigian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied appellant's petition for writ of mandate to compel respondent state bar to withdraw its finding that appellant had committed dishonest conduct in wrongfully taking money from a client and not pursuing the claim or refunding the money.


OVERVIEW: Client hired appellant attorney to represent him in a malpractice action against his former attorneys. Appellant filed a complaint for legal malpractice but he filed no further documents and made no appearances. As a result, the action was dismissed by the trial court for lack of prosecution. Client sought reimbursement on the basis that appellant had neither pursued the claim nor refunded the money. The Client Security Fund Commission, a division of respondent state bar, instituted an investigation and subsequently issued a decision proposing reimbursement of the unearned balance of the payment made to appellant. Appellant contended that the client's payment was a fee for consultation and petitioned for a writ of mandate in the trial court. The trial court affirmed the findings. The evidence showed that appellant's acts fell within the concept of the wrongful taking of a client's money. Further, appellant failed to utilize the client's funds for the purpose for which they were tendered. The court also found that de novo review was not appropriate when an administrative decision did not involve a fundamental right, and it found respondent's actions appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied appellant attorney's petition for writ of mandate to compel respondent state bar to withdraw a finding that appellant had committed dishonest conduct, because the evidence showed that appellant's acts fell within the concept of the wrongful taking of a client's money, and it showed that appellant failed to utilized client's funds for the purpose which they were tendered.

 

1063 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Fisher


No. A054733


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


12 Cal. App. 4th 1556; 15 Cal. Rptr. 2d 889; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 92; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 795; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1493; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1579



February 1, 1993, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * ]


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I, III, and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County, No. 12128, Beverly B. Savitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which convicted him for two counts of violating Cal. Penal Code § 422, threatening another with death or great bodily injury under certain circumstances, and two counts of violating Cal. Penal Code § 242, misdemeanor battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for two counts of violating Cal. Penal Code § 422, threatening another with death or great bodily injury under certain circumstances, and two counts of violating Cal. Penal Code § 242, misdemeanor battery. On appeal, defendant contended that § 422 was unconstitutionally overbroad because it did not require that the speaker intend to carry out the threat. The court held that a threat which the speaker did not intend to implement was not speech protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The court found that proof of specific intent to carry out the threat was not constitutionally compelled, so long as the threat on its face and in the circumstances in which it was made was so unequivocal, unconditional, immediate, and specific as to the person threatened, as to convey a gravity of purpose and imminent prospect of execution. The court then affirmed defendant's convictions, holding that it was readily apparent that § 422 was not unconstitutionally overbroad and that it had been carefully drafted to comport with detailed guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for threatening another with death or great bodily injury, holding that a threat which the speaker did not intend to implement was not constitutionally protected speech. Proof of intent to carry out the threat was unnecessary if the threat and the circumstances in which it had been made conveyed a gravity of purpose and prospect of execution. The court also affirmed convictions for misdemeanor battery.

Estate of Ruchti


No. B054773


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


12 Cal. App. 4th 1593; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 151; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 97; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 838; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1571



February 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified February 23, 1993. Rehearing Denied February 16, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 163. Review Denied April 21, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2207.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. SOP39345, William E. McGinley, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Sanctions on appeal are awarded to respondents against appellant in the amount of $ 10,000. Costs on appeal are awarded to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, attorney for a suspended co-executor of the deceased, sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which upheld a protective order and the awarding of sanctions against appellant for his misconduct in discovery proceedings with respect to the administration of the deceased's will.


OVERVIEW: The attorney of respondents, co-executors of the deceased, was issued a subpoena for his own deposition by appellant, attorney for a suspended co-executor. After a court hearing, respondents' attorney mailed a meet-and-confer letter to appellant, to which appellant did not respond. The lower court issued a protective order and imposed sanctions on appellant for his failure to comply with its discovery procedures. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court noted that there was evidence that respondents' attorney misrepresented his relationship with the judge in order to have the judge recused from the probate proceedings, but it held that there existed other discovery techniques to elicit the information requested by appellant. The decision of the lower court was neither arbitrary nor capricious and the court affirmed that, as such, it was not determined to be an abuse of discretion. The court further issued sanctions against appellant for what it considered a frivolous appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court because appellant, attorney for a suspended co-executor of the deceased, attempted to improperly utilize unnecessary discovery methods with respect to the administration of the deceased's will, from which sanctions were correctly imposed. The court also imposed sanctions on appellant for which it determined to be a frivolous appeal.

People v. Woods


No. A055941, No. A056503


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


12 Cal. App. 4th 1139; 15 Cal. Rptr. 2d 906; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 183; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 796; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1507



February 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 22, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2252. Mosk, J., is of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Solano County, No. C-31256, James F. Moelk, Judge.



DISPOSITION: On the appeal, the order dismissing the information is reversed. On the petition for writ of habeas corpus, the order to show cause is discharged, and the petition is denied as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Solano County (California), which dismissed a murder prosecution against respondent accused and denied appellant a third filing of the charges under Cal. Penal Code § 1387.1. Respondent filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state twice dismissed criminal charges against respondent accused due to clerical errors in one of the counts. The municipal court granted appellant's motion to file charges a third time, and respondent filed a de novo motion to dismiss under Cal. Penal Code § 1387. The superior court dismissed, holding that there was not sufficient evidence of "excusable neglect" to allow a third filing. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the municipal court had heard the evidence and that the superior court should not have substituted its judgment for that of the municipal court. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was therefore moot. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 1387.1 created an exception to the general rule of § 1387 that a charge could not be filed a third time and allowed a third filing where either of the prior dismissals was due solely to excusable neglect and the state's conduct did not amount to bad faith. Bad faith had not been alleged. The municipal court had not abused its discretion when it found that appellant's error was excusable, because a reasonably prudent person under the same or similar circumstances might have made the same error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's order, which had dismissed appellant state's murder prosecution against respondent accused, and denied as moot respondent's petition for writ of habeas corpus. The court held that appellant could file murder and special circumstances charges against respondent a third time because the previous two dismissals were due to excusable neglect and bad faith was not alleged.

 

1066 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Nick v. Department of Motor Vehicles


No. A054300


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE.


12 Cal. App. 4th 1407; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 305; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 87; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1428; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 740



January 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 13, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2543.
Panelli, J., and Kennard, J., are of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 928337, Ralph J. Flageolett, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: We hold that appellant received a full and fair administrative hearing and that the evidence supports the conclusion that appellant drove with a blood-alcohol level of .08 percent or more. The judgment of the trial court dismissing appellant's petition for a writ of mandate is affirmed. Each party will bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver contested the dismissal of a petition for a writ of mandate by the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), ordering respondents, Department of Motor Vehicles and Highway Patrol, to reinstate his driver's license. Appellant claimed he was denied a fair hearing under Cal. Gov't Code § 68097.2(b), and that the evidence did not support the trial court's conclusion.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, Department of Motor Vehicles and Highway Patrol, suspended the driver's license of appellant driver for drunk driving. Appellant contended that he was denied a fair hearing because he was unable to compel the attendance of the arresting officer due to his indigence, and that the evidence did not support the conclusion that he had been driving drunk. The court rejected both arguments and affirmed the judgment. It held that appellant had not complied with Cal. Gov't Code § 68097.2(b) that required him to reimburse respondent Highway Patrol for the expense of a peace officer's salary, in order for the officer to comply with appellant's subpoena, and that § 68097.2(b) did not infringe on appellant's due process rights. The court held that the privilege of operating a motor vehicle was important, but not fundamental. Appellant had shown a lack of due diligence to support his claim at the hearing, when he failed to attempt to have the subpoena fee waived or to have the subpoena enforced. The court held that there was no error in the trial court's admission of evidence of appellant's blood alcohol level, or its determination that appellant had been driving drunk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant driver's petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondents, Department of Motor Vehicles and Highway Patrol, to reinstate his driver's license. It held that appellant had not complied with subpoena requirements, and did not exercise due diligence in claiming indigence. Appellant's due process rights were not violated, and the trial court did not err in finding that appellant was driving drunk.

Provigo Corp. v. Alcoholic Beverage Etc. App. Bd.


No. A058137, No. A058534


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


18 Cal. App. 4th 255; 15 Cal. Rptr. 2d 886; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 69; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 709; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1271



January 27, 1993, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted April 29, 1993 (S031492), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2437.
Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 12 Cal. App. 4th 1205.)


PRIOR HISTORY: A058137: Alcoholic Beverage Appeals Bd. No. AB-6067.

A058534: Alcoholic Beverage Appeals Bd. No. AB-6200



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the board are reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner grocery stores appealed a judgment by respondent Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board (California), that suspended petitioners' licenses for selling alcohol to minors in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 25658(a), alleging that the practice of using underage police decoys to attempt to purchase alcohol in order to enforce the prohibition of selling alcohol to minors was a violation of Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22.


OVERVIEW: Law enforcement agencies utilized underage decoys in supervised programs to enforce the prohibition against selling alcohol to minors, pursuant to Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22 and Cal. Bus. & Prof. § 25658(a). The California Department of Alcohol Beverage Control (department) suspended the licenses of petitioner grocery stores. Petitioners protested their license suspensions and argued that the use of underage police agents to purchase alcoholic beverages was unconstitutional. Respondent California Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board interpreted the constitutional provision that "no person under the age of 21 years shall purchase any alcoholic beverage" (Cal. Const., art. XX, § 22) to exclude persons in decoy programs supervised by the department or other law enforcement agency. On appeal, the court reversed respondent's judgment and found that, unlike Cal. Heath & Safety Code § 11367, both the constitutional provision and the statute covering the prohibition against buying alcohol contained no express exception for persons working in a law enforcement capacity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the alcohol license suspensions of petitioner grocery stores by respondent California Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board because it was impermissible under the California constitution to use underage youths as decoys in the enforcement of the prohibition against selling alcohol to minors.

 

1068 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Monroe


No. A053694


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


12 Cal. App. 4th 1174; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 267; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 74; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 700; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1333



January 27, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 29, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2447.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 105811, William A. McKinstry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of cocaine base for sale, pursuant to Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351.5, after the vehicle defendant was traveling in was stopped, an open container was observed at defendant's feet, and defendant was arrested and searched when he failed to present any identification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine base for sale under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351.5. Defendant appealed his conviction on grounds that the cocaine should have been suppressed because Cal. Veh. Code § 40302(a) was unconstitutional, and thus the search of defendant was illegal. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that the officer's decision to take defendant who had no identification into custody was a proper exercise of his discretion under Cal. Veh. Code § 40302. Cal. Veh. Code § 40302 delegates discretion to an officer, after arresting an individual for a minor vehicle code violation, to either cite and release, or take into custody, an individual where he does not have a driver's license or its functional equivalent, based on the officer's determination of whether other evidence of identification presented was satisfactory. Cal. Veh. Code § 40302 is not fatally vague and unconstitutional for giving an officer such discretion. An officer must accept, as satisfactory evidence of identification, any current written identification which bears the minimum amount of data required by Cal. Veh. Code § 12811 and § 40500.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, because the officer's decision to take defendant into custody, resulting in a search, was a proper exercise of discretion where defendant could not produce a driver's license or other satisfactory evidence of identification.

 

1069 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Halsey


No. B065728


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


12 Cal. App. 4th 885; 16 Cal. Rptr. 2d 47; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 56; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 574; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1125



January 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. LA004972, Leon S. Kaplan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), for voluntary manslaughter, under Cal. Penal Code § 192(a), while using a firearm, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12022.5, and was sentenced to state prison for 10 years.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction in trial court for voluntary manslaughter while using a firearm and was sentenced to 10 years in prison. Appellant contended that the trial court erred by giving Cal. Evid. Code § 1103 regarding admission of character evidence for violence ex post facto application. The court rejected appellant's ex post facto claim because he did not object at trial, and additionally, appellant called the court's attention to the amended statute and urged its application as part of his trial strategy to show that victim was violent. The court held that admission of testimony concerning appellant's interest in guns was not error because he did not object at trial and also held that officer's testimony concerning appellant's statement was admissible. The court disagreed with appellant's contention that dismissal of a juror was error because the trial court had discretion to dismiss the juror for violating the trial court's order to discuss the case and for failure to follow instructions. Accordingly the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because application of amended statute was not error, witness testimony was admissible, and the trial court had the discretion to dismiss a juror for good cause.

People v. Cabral


No. F017396


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


12 Cal. App. 4th 820; 15 Cal. Rptr. 2d 866; 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 48; 93 Cal. Daily Op. Service 546; 93 Daily Journal DAR 1003



January 22, 1993, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 ]


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976. This opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Stanislaus County No. 268489, Aldo Girolami, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction of violation of Penal Code section 288.5 is reversed, and the case is remanded for resentencing. In all other respects the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant suspect sought review of his convictions in the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California) for numerous counts of sexual misconduct involving children.


OVERVIEW: Appellant suspect was convicted of numerous counts of penetration by a foreign object, sodomy, rape, oral copulation upon a child under the age of 14, lewd or lascivious acts upon a child under 14, and continuous sexual abuse of a child. Appellant argued that his convictions were improper because the trial court committed prejudicial error in allowing into evidence a letter from appellant to a psychotherapist in which he admitted acts of sexual molestation. The reviewing court upheld most counts of the conviction. To determine if the letter was a confidential communication between patient and psychotherapist under Cal. Evid. Code § 1014, the reviewing court applied the dominant purpose test. Here, appellant's asserted purpose was to avoid a prison sentence, not to receive treatment. Even assuming that the letter was privileged, appellant was not prejudiced, given the ample evidence.


OUTCOME: Appellant suspect's convictions for numerous counts of sexual misconduct involving children were affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded because a letter that appellant wrote was not a confidential communication with a psychotherapist and was admissible.

People v. Serrano

COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE

DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for numerous crimes, including kidnapping for ransom in a manner which exposed the victim to a substantial likelihood of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with several crimes including kidnapping for ransom in a manner which exposed his victim to a substantial likelihood of death. The defense consisted of the testimony of a participant in the crime, who claimed he had kidnapped the victim in retaliation for threats from her family to his. Defendant claimed he knew nothing of the kidnapping until he arrived at location where the victim was held and that his cohort told him that the victim had committed a crime in defendant's home. Defendant claimed he asked the victim to return his stolen belongings, allegedly as ransom, but that he wanted no part in the kidnapping. Defendant was convicted of the crimes by a jury and appealed his conviction. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court properly rejected defendant's claim that he had a good faith claim to the ransom demanded. The court also found that the statute under which defendant was convicted was not constitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for crimes including kidnapping for ransom in a manner which exposed his victim to a substantial likelihood of death, because the statute governing such an act was not constitutionally vague. The court rejected defendant's argument that he had a good faith claim to the ransom demanded of the victim.

People v. Gandotra


No. B051942


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


11 Cal. App. 4th 1355; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 896; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1489; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 10362; 92 Daily Journal DAR 17364



December 23, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * ]


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III through V.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied April 21, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 2206.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. A 481115 and A 481141, Charles E. Frisco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We modify the judgment against Dr. Gandotra by staying the fines and penalty assessments imposed on counts 2, 5, 7, 9, and 11 through 15, and direct the trial court on remand to recalculate the new total of fines and assessments owed. As modified, the judgments against both defendants are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physician and his wife sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), convicting defendant physician of aiding and abetting his unlicensed assistant in the prescribing and furnishing of controlled substances under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11153(a) and Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11352(a), and convicting defendants of Medi-Cal fraud under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1407.


OVERVIEW: Defendant physician was convicted of aiding and abetting an unlicensed assistant to prescribe and dispense a controlled substance under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11153(a) and Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11352, and defendant physician and his wife were convicted for Medi-Cal fraud under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 14107. The court found that Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11153 prohibited an unlicensed assistant from writing a controlled substance prescription, without regard to whether the prescription was medically appropriate, and that defendant physician's convictions under § 11153(a) for aiding and abetting an unlicensed assistant to write prescriptions, were supported by substantial evidence. Defendant physician could not rely on the medical appropriateness of the unlicensed assistant's illegal prescription to escape liability under § 11352 because the assistant was not a licensed physician. The court modified the judgment against defendant physician by staying fines and penalty assessments that violated Cal. Penal Code § 654, and directed the trial court to recalculate the new total of fines and assessments owed. As modified, the court affirmed the judgments against defendants.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment against defendant physician by staying some of the fines and penalty assessments, and directed the trial court to recalculate the new total owed. As modified, the court affirmed the judgments against defendant physician and his wife. The court found substantial evidence that defendant physician aided and abetted an unlicensed assistant in writing prescriptions for controlled substances.

 

1073 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



County of Los Angeles v. Patrick


No. B060521


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


11 Cal. App. 4th 1246; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 665; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1472; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 10249; 92 Daily Journal DAR 17113



December 21, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. CSD 000120, James D. Endman, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded to the trial court to redetermine the proper amount of child support in accordance with the views expressed herein. Plaintiff shall bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which modified the amount of child support payable by defendant father and held that Cal. R. Ct. 1274(b)(6) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county sought a modification of child support concerning defendant father's payments in support of his minor child, who was in its mother's custody and received welfare benefits. The lower court ordered an increase in child support and held that Cal. Civ. Code §1274(b)(6) unconstitutionally discriminated against noncustodial parents on the basis of wealth. Plaintiff county appealed, contending that Cal. Civ. Code §1274(b)(6) was constitutional and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Cal. Const. art. I § 7(a). The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, holding that Cal. Civ. Code § 1274(b)(6) made a classification based on the welfare status of the child that was subject to the rational basis test. Accordingly, a legitimate purpose existed for distinguishing between noncustodial parents of children whose custodial parents received welfare benefits and noncustodial parents generally, in allowing a reduction in support based on visitation. The state's interest in relieving the public of the economic burden of support for needy children was legitimate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which modified defendant father's child support and found that a statute was unconstitutional, and remanded the case for determination of the proper amount of child support, because it was constitutional under the Equal Protection clause for the state to consider the welfare status of a dependent child in determining child support.

Safeco Ins. Co. v. Garamendi


No. B063893.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


27 Cal. App. 4th 400; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 621; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1459; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 10170; 92 Daily Journal DAR 17076



December 17, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted March 25, 1993 (S030921), Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 1766.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court(See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 16 Cal.App.4th 1596 and 21 Cal. App. 4th 1428.)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC004816, Dzintra I. Janavs, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed as moot. Appellant insurers are to bear all costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurers sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied their motions for writs of mandamus or mandate and to enjoin respondent state insurance commissioner from holding company-specific hearings on insurance rate rollbacks.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurers filed motions for writs of mandate and for injunctive relief, seeking to prevent respondent state insurance commissioner from holding company-specific hearings on insurance rate rollbacks. The trial court denied appellants' motions. The court dismissed appellants' case as moot. It held that the former state insurance commissioner's decision was not adjudicatory but was quasi-legislative in nature and, thus, was lawfully reconsidered, rescinded, and superseded by new and different regulations regarding generic ratesetting issues of general applicability. The court found that by validly rescinding the decision and superseding it with new and different regulations, respondent had effectively accorded appellants the relief they requested. The court concluded that the decision was validly rescinded by respondent and, thus, that appellants had administratively obtained the relief they requested.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant insurers' requests for mandate and injunctive relief as moot and found that the decision of the predecessor of respondent state insurance commissioner was not adjudicatory, but was quasi-legislative in nature. The court held that by validly rescinding his predecessor's decision, respondent had effectively accorded appellants the relief that they had requested.

 

1075 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Morehart v. County of Santa Barbara


No. B058957.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


21 Cal. App. 4th 1401; 15 Cal. Rptr. 2d 212; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1443; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 10062; 92 Daily Journal DAR 16748



December 14, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing January 11, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. App. LEXIS 19. Review Granted March 11, 1993 (S030829), Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 1323.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court(See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 16 Cal.App.4th 1560.)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Barbara County, No. 17674, William L. Gordon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We uphold the validity of the Antiquated Subdivision Zoning Ordinances and reverse the trial court's judgment. Costs to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county and board of supervisors, sought review from the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which held that appellant's zoning ordinances, commonly referred to as the Antiquated Subdivision Ordinances, were preempted by the exclusive merger provisions of the state Subdivision Map Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 66451.10-66451.21, and therefore were invalid and unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, county and board of supervisors, contended that the trial court erred when it determined that the local zoning ordinance was preempted by the merger provisions in the Subdivision Map Act (Map Act), Cal. Gov't Code § 66451.10-66451.21. Appellees owned a 3.7-acre parcel. In 1981, appellant downzoned the area so that only 1 dwelling per 100 acres was permitted, however there was a grandfather clause. Appellees filed for a permit to build on the parcel and appellants' denied the request. Appellants contended that it was feasible to recombine appellee's parcel with enough contiguous lots to make a 100-acre parcel because the other lots were owned by appellees' family or their corporation. The trial court concluded that the county ordinances were preempted by the exclusive merger provisions of the Map Act. The court stated that although the Map Act controlled development of parcels in a broad sense, the Map Act permitted the local governments to supplement it with reasonable local regulations. The court held that the local government was not precluded from controlling development of substandard parcels simply because the end result was a merger of parcels.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment that the California Subdivision Map Act preempted the local zoning ordinances was reversed and remanded. The court held that the California Subdivision Map Act expressly permitted the local governments to supplement it with reasonable local regulations.

 

1076 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Murphy v. City of Alameda


No. A056245


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


11 Cal. App. 4th 906; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 329; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1438; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 10058; 92 Daily Journal DAR 16753



December 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 11, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 1331.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 620918-8, James R. Lambden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, and the matter remanded for a trial on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Alameda County (California), which was entered in favor of defendant city on plaintiffs' motion for summary adjudication of issues and which determined that Cal. Evid. Code § 669.5 did not apply in plaintiffs' action challenging the validity of defendant's municipal ordinance prohibiting the development of multiple dwelling units.


OVERVIEW: In 1973, pursuant to the amendment of defendant city's charter by the voters, defendant enacted an ordinance prohibiting the building of multiple dwelling units. In 1981, Cal. Evid. Code § 669.5 went into effect, shifting the burden of proof in actions challenging the validity of certain growth control ordinances to the proponents of those ordinances. In 1987, plaintiffs filed suit against defendant and challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance prohibiting the building of multiple dwelling units. Plaintiffs moved for summary adjudication of issues, seeking a determination that § 669.5 applied to their action. The trial court held that § 669.5 did not apply and entered judgment in defendant's favor. Plaintiffs appealed. On review, the court reversed and remanded the case for a trial on the merits. The court held that § 669.5 was applicable in plaintiffs' action and that the ordinance fell within the scope of § 669.5. Because § 669.5 addressed the conduct of trials and did not change the legal consequences of the parties' past conduct, the statute's operation was prospective. In any event, the statute's language suggested that the statute was intended to apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that the statute at issue did not apply to plaintiff claimants' action challenging the validity of defendant city's municipal ordinance prohibiting the development of multiple dwelling units. The case was remanded for a trial on the merits, and, pursuant to the statute at issue, the burden of proof was shifted to defendant.

Nick v. Department of Motor Vehicles


No. A054300


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE.


11 Cal. App. 4th 868; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 290; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1432; 92 Daily Journal DAR 16652; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9980



December 11, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted January 5, 1993. (See 12 Cal. App. 4th 1407)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 928337, Ralph J. Flageolett, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: We hold that appellant received a full and fair administrative hearing and affirm the judgment of the trial court dismissing his petition for a writ of mandate. Costs are awarded to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that dismissed appellant's petition for writ of mandate directed against respondents, the California Department of Motor Vehicles and the California Highway Patrol. Appellant asserted he was denied a fair hearing on the suspension of his driver's license.


OVERVIEW: After his driver's license was suspended in an administrative hearing, appellant filed a petition for a writ or mandate directed against respondents, the state department of motor vehicles and the state highway patrol. Appellant sought reinstatement of his driver's license. The trial court dismissed the petition and appellant sought review, contending he was denied a fair hearing on the suspension of his driver's license because he was unable, due to his indigence, to compel the attendance of the arresting officer. The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant's petition because it held that the suspension of driving privileges was a civil matter that was independent of the person's guilt or innocence in any parallel criminal prosecution. The court also held that the privilege to drive a motor vehicle was not a fundamental right and that a driver was required to pay fees in connection therewith. Finally, the court noted that appellant had not exercised due diligence in invoking the court's aid to secure his witness and that he therefore did not have room to complain of the absence of the witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's petition for a writ of mandate because it found that appellant could not complain of the absence of a witness when he failed to exercise due diligence in enlisting the court's aid to secure the witness.

Bravo Vending v. City of Rancho Mirage


No. E009290


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


11 Cal. App. 4th 585; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 209; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1407; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9817; 92 Daily Journal DAR 16352



December 7, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted January 4, 1993 (See 16 Cal. App. 4th 383).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, Nos. Indio 63521 and 63522, Richard Lee, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: Since preemption is the sole reason advanced for the Ordinance's alleged invalidity, the trial court's judgment that the Ordinance is valid must be affirmed. Our order staying the enforcement of the Ordinance is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vending company sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), denying both appellant's petition for writ of mandate and an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court determined that Cal. Penal Code § 308 did not preempt the city's prohibition of cigarette vending machines.


OVERVIEW: Appellant vending company sought a writ of mandate and filed an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from a city ordinance, Rancho Mirage, Cal., Municipal Code ch. 5.24, which prohibited cigarette vending machines. The trial court denied both types of relief, finding that Cal. Penal Code § 308 did not preempt the ordinance. The court affirmed, finding that the ordinance was not preempted because it did not duplicate any provision of § 308, nor did the ordinance contradict § 308 because § 308 did not expressly authorize the use of vending machines for cigarette sales. The court found that § 308 did not occupy the entire field. Finally, the court found that appellant did not meet its burden to show that § 308 preempted the ordinance because the laws did not concern the same subject matter. Although § 308 concerned sale of cigarettes to minors, the ordinance concerned sale of cigarettes in vending machines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the ordinance was valid because preemption was the sole reason advanced for the ordinance's alleged invalidity and the state statute did not preempt the ordinance.

People v. Wallace


No. F015756


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


11 Cal. App. 4th 568; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 67; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1403; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9781; 92 Daily Journal DAR 16279



December 4, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Kern County, No. 43833A, James M. Stuart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The convictions on counts I, II, and III are reversed. The conviction on count V is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed child molestation convictions in the Superior Court of Kern County (California), under Cal. Penal Code §§ 288(c), 311.4(c), and 647.6. Defendant contended that neither his or the victims' conduct as depicted on the videotape constituted lewd or lascivious acts or sexual conduct, that he lacked specific intent, and that jury instructions incorrectly defined the crimes charged.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions under Cal. Penal Code § 288(c), a lewd and lascivious act upon a minor by a person with the intent of arousing, appealing to, or gratifying the lust or passions or sexual desires of that person or of the child, Cal. Penal Code § 311.4(c), inducing a minor to engage in preparing a film involving sexual conduct, and Cal. Penal Code § 647.6, annoying or molesting of children under the age of 18. The court reversed the convictions under § 288(c) and § 311.4(c), while affirming the § 647.6 conviction. The court found that defendant did not directly touch the victims and did not indirectly touch them in a lewd or lascivious manner. The victims remained clothed and did not engage in sexual acts. Violations could not occur without a sexual act. The court held that it was reversible error not to instruct the jury that an essential element of § 288(c) and § 311.4(c) was that the defendant's touching of the victims had to be lewd and lascivious, regardless of his specific intent. Such an instructional error was not harmless under the applicable "beyond a reasonable doubt" standard.


OUTCOME: The convictions for committing a lewd and lascivious act upon a minor with the intent of arousing, appealing to, or gratifying the lust or passions or sexual desires of that person or of the child, and for inducing a minor to engage in preparing a film involving sexual conduct, were reversed. A lewd and lascivious act was not proven where there was no proof of sexual conduct or specific intent. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Texas Commerce Bank v. Garamendi


Nos. B064437, B064620, B064871


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR

DISPOSITION: The judgment entered June 11, 1992, is affirmed to the extent it determines the 1986 Muni-GICs owners are entitled to class-5 priority as "policyholders."


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from a declaratory judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that purchasers of municipal bond guaranteed investment contracts from an insolvent insurer had preferred class-5 claim priority in insolvency proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The trustees in insolvency proceedings for an insurance company filed an action for declaratory relief to determine whether purchasers of municipal bond guaranteed investment contracts (Muni-GICs) from the insolvent insurer were entitled to preferred class-5 claim priority as insurance policyholders in the insolvency proceedings. The trial court found that purchasers of Muni-GICs had preferred class-5 claim priority. The appellate court affirmed, holding that because Muni-GICs were annuities-certain and Cal. Ins. Code § 101 classifies annuities as a type of insurance, the purchasers of Muni-GICs received preferred claim status as insurance policyholders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment because municipal bond guaranteed investment contracts are annuities-certain and are classified as a type of insurance.

Barclays Bank Internat. Ltd. v. Franchise Tax Bd.


No. C003388


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


10 Cal. App. 4th 1742; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 537; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1350; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9447; 92 Daily Journal DAR 15619



November 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 18, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1467. Certiorari Granted November 1, 1993, 62 U.S.L. Week 3319 [126 L.Ed 2d 329, 114 S. Ct. 379].


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Nos. 325059 and 325061, George E. Paras, Judge. * 


* Retired Associate Justice of the Court of Appeal, Third District, sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, and the trial court is directed to enter a judgment for Board. Each party shall bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant California Franchise Tax Board appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which held that a regulation for the allocation of income of foreign-based companies, such as plaintiff foreign-based corporation, was a violation of due process.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff foreign-based corporation filed suit against defendant California Franchise Tax Board when defendant used the worldwide combined reporting (WWCR) method of income allocation, codified at Cal. Code Regs. tit. 18, § 25137-6, to levy additional taxes on plaintiff. After the California Supreme Court reversed and remanded the court's judgment that WWCR was unconstitutional, the court held that the WWCR method violated neither the Commerce nor Due Process Clauses of the U.S. Constitution. The court found that WWCR was not discriminatory under the Commerce Clause because domestic- and foreign-based corporations stood on relatively equal footing when one considered the "practical operation" of the method as applied to the compliance costs they incurred. The court held that WWCR was permissible under federal and state Due Process clauses because defendant's discretion regarding compliance cost computation under regulation § 25137-6 was subject to reasonably adequate standards to guide enforcement. The court therefore reversed the judgment of the trial court that § 25137-6 violated due process protections and remanded with direction to enter judgment for defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that the unitary tax method of worldwide combined reporting as applied to plaintiff foreign-based corporation violated due process protections, because adequate safeguards controlled defendant California Franchise Tax Board's regulatory discretion in computing compliance costs; the court therefore remanded the case with instructions that judgment be entered for defendant.

 

1082 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Colgate-Palmolive Co. v. Franchise Tax Bd.


No. C007044


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


10 Cal. App. 4th 1768; 13 Cal. Rptr. 2d 761; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1358; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9458; 92 Daily Journal DAR 15586



November 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted November 1, 1993, 62 U.S.L. Week 3319 [126 L.Ed 2d 329, 114 S. Ct. 379].


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 319715, Robert Gardner, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The portion of the judgment regarding the foreign commerce clause issue is reversed. The portion of the judgment regarding the constitutional and statutory distortion issues and on the matter of sanctions is affirmed. The Board is awarded its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The California Supreme Court remanded the case to the appeals court so that the appeals court could modify its previous decision that California's worldwide unitary tax method, Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 25101, which allocated a tax on respondent corporation, was not unconstitutional so that the decision would be consistent with a recent decision of the California Supreme Court .


OVERVIEW: Appellant Franchise Tax Board sought review of a trial court decision that the method which appellant used to compute taxes owed by respondent corporation was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court originally held that the method was not unconstitutional. However, the state supreme court remanded for a modification so the decision would be consistent with a recent state supreme court decision. On remand, the court held that the method was not unconstitutional because there was an affirmative federal policy permitting California to apply the worldwide unitary tax method to domestic-parent groups with foreign subsidiaries. Thus, there was no need to apply the dormant foreign commerce clause framework because Congress has acted and the courts were no longer needed to prevent states from burdening commerce. The court held that respondent did not meet the steep burden imposed by the constitutional distortion principle of "external consistency." The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied appellant's motion for sanctions because the motion was not timely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its decision and reversed the decision of the trial court because a constitutional analysis was not necessary because there was an affirmative federal policy which allowed California to apply the worldwide unitary tax method to domestic-parent groups with foreign subsidiaries.

 

1083 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



American Drug Stores, Inc. v. Stroh


No. D015010


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


10 Cal. App. 4th 1446; 13 Cal. Rptr. 2d 432; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1319; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9218; 92 Daily Journal DAR 15309



November 13, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. EC003302, Robert E. May, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant liquor licensee sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), that sustained the demurrer of appellee state alcoholic beverage control department to appellant's complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief seeking to prevent appellee from imposing penalties based on the results of a sting operation.The trial court sustained the demurrer without leave to amend.


OVERVIEW: Appellant liquor licensee filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief, along with a motion for a preliminary injunction, seeking to prevent appellee state alcoholic beverage control department from imposing any penalties based on the results of a sting operation where sales were made to minors who acted as undercover agents. Appellee demurred to the complaint on the ground that the superior court lacked jurisdiction under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 23090.5, to entertain the complaint or grant the requested relief, and the trial court sustained the demurrer without leave to amend. The court affirmed and held that the statutory scheme comprehensively vested exclusive jurisdiction for judicial review of such disciplinary action in the supreme court and appellate courts by way of writ review. In that the thrust of appellant's action was to disable appellee from taking disciplinary action, such a judgment on its face would have violated the proscriptions of § 23090.5 because it would have annulled an order or decision in advance, or at minimum would have restrained, enjoined, or interfered with the department in the performance of its duties.


OUTCOME: The order sustaining appellee state alcoholic beverage control department's demurrer without leave to amend was affirmed because the superior court lacked jurisdiction to grant appellant liquor licensee's requested relief. The court held that the statutory scheme comprehensively vested exclusive jurisdiction for judicial review of appellee's disciplinary action in the supreme court and appellate courts by way of writ review.

 

1084 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Deskin


No. F015872


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


10 Cal. App. 4th 1397; 13 Cal. Rptr. 2d 391; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1311; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9174; 92 Daily Journal DAR 15205



November 10, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of the Statement of Facts and part I.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 44007, Leonard M. McGillivray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by a jury in the Superior Court, Kern County (California) of the misdemeanor offense of child endangerment in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 273a(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the misdemeanor offense of child endangerment in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 273a(2), a lesser included offense of felony child endangerment, § 273a(1). On appeal, defendant contended § 273a(1) was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that § 273a(2) was not unconstitutionally vague for the same reasoning that § 273a(1) has been held not void for vagueness. The court found that violation of § 273a required proof of criminal negligence. This meant that defendant's conduct must be a reckless, gross, or culpable departure from what would be the conduct of an ordinarily prudent person under the same situation as to be incompatible with proper regard for human life. The court determined that parents and others under this standard should be able to tell the difference between criminal and noncriminal behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of the misdemeanor offense of child endangerment because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague in that it held every person to an objective standard of reasonableness regarding causing physical pain, mental suffering, or injury to the child, or the endangering of the child's person or health.

People v. Blanco


No. A054352


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


10 Cal. App. 4th 1167; 13 Cal. Rptr. 2d 176; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1293; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9058; 92 Daily Journal DAR 14955



November 4, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 139159, Lenard D. Louie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment by the San Francisco Superior Court (California), which convicted him of second-degree murder with the use of a firearm, and imposed a sentence of 15 years to life plus four years for the use of the firearm.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of second-degree murder for shooting the victim in the back after a botched drug deal. At trial, evidence was admitted that tended to show that appellant had a reputation for violence. Appellant contended that Cal. Evid. Code § 1103(b) violated his due process rights by making evidence of his reputation for violence admissible when he had not proffered evidence as to his reputation for or character trait of violence. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that § 1103(b) was constitutionally applied in appellant's case, because § 1103(b) allowed such evidence in rebuttal to defense evidence. Therefore, there was no violation of constitutional principles of due process. The court further concluded that if there had been a constitutional error, on the facts of the particular case, the error would have been harmless.


OUTCOME: Appellant's second-degree murder conviction was affirmed. Appellant's constitutional due process challenge was dismissed, because the evidence admitted at trial relating to appellant's reputation for violence was offered in rebuttal to defense evidence. Thus, there was no violation of the state or the federal constitution.

City of Costa Mesa v. Soffer


No. G011395


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


11 Cal. App. 4th 378; 13 Cal. Rptr. 2d 735; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1370; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9530; 92 Daily Journal DAR 15841



October 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Ordered Published November 25, 1992. Review Denied February 10, 1993, Reported at 1993 Cal. LEXIS 675.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. X 631808, Richard O. Frazee, Sr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which declared five of appellant's motor vehicles a public nuisance pursuant to Costa Mesa, Cal., Municipal Code § 11-65 et seq., and required him to obtain a certificate of compliance for a sixth.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owner stored several vehicles without current registrations at his residence, not in any structure. Respondent city filed a complaint, seeking to declare the vehicles a nuisance, pursuant to Costa Mesa, Cal., Municipal Code § 11-65, and seeking injunctive and declaratory relief to abate the vehicles as a public nuisance. The court declared five of the vehicles a public nuisance and ordered them to be removed within 10 days. The court affirmed, finding that respondent could declare abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, or inoperative vehicles or parts thereof on private property a public nuisance and could declare certain uses of property a nuisance per se. The court held that respondent successfully carried its burden of proving the vehicles were a public nuisance because they were abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, or inoperative. The court held that Costa Mesa, Cal., Municipal Code § 11-65 et seq., was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court found that Costa Mesa, Cal., Municipal Code §§ 11-68 and 11-69 did not violate the warrant requirement of U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of respondent city. The court held that respondent had the authority to declare abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, or inoperative cars as public nuisances and successfully proved that appellant owner's vehicles were nuisances under the ordinance.

Colony Cove Ass'n v. City of Carson


No. B062956


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


10 Cal. App. 4th 1646; 14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 849; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1347; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9370; 92 Daily Journal DAR 15558



October 22, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified November 19, 1992. Review Denied February 11, 1993 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1993 Cal. LEXIS 733.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. SCC024690, Irving S. Feffer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Each party is to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobilehome park owner sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted judgment on the pleadings to respondent city in appellant's suit challenging respondent's rent control ordinance on the grounds that the ordinance did not constitute a physical taking requiring just compensation and that the statute of limitations barred appellant's claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mobilehome park owner filed suit challenging respondent city's rent control ordinance, alleging that the ordinance effected a taking of its property without just compensation by failing to include a "vacancy decontrol" provision that would allow appellant to charge market rents to a successor tenant if a current tenant sold his or her mobilehome. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to respondent. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that appellant had stated a claim that the ordinance was an unconstitutional taking, because it alleged that the ordinance worked to increase the cost of mobilehome housing to all tenants except those in place at the time it was enacted, which was contrary to the ordinance's purpose. The court also held that the statute of limitations did not bar appellant's action, because each sale of a mobilehome constituted a separate taking, a new limitations period thus commenced with the sale of each home located in appellant's park, and appellant's claim for damages were limited to those home sold within the five years preceding its filing of its complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of judgment on the pleadings to respondent city on appellant mobilehome park owner's claim that respondent's rent control ordinance constituted a taking, because appellant stated a claim by alleging that the ordinance actually increased costs for tenants, which was contrary to the ordinance's purpose, and the statute of limitations began to run upon each sale of a home in appellant's park and thus had not expired.

In re Ricky H.


No. E009488


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


10 Cal. App. 4th 552; 12 Cal. Rptr. 2d 578; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1231; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8605; 92 Daily Journal DAR 14187



October 16, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Superior Court of Riverside County, No. J-70231. Stephen D. Cunnison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged judgments from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) over findings made pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.21 and Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26 in a parental termination proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother challenged orders entered by the trial court on March 12, 1991 setting a dispositional hearing, the first appeal, and on July 12, 1991, which terminated parents' rights to son and placed daughter in long term foster care. The court had previously dismissed as untimely the second appeal. The court dismissed the first appeal refusing to deem the first notice of appeal to be a premature appeal because such appeals were timely when the decision being appealed from had been made preliminarily, but was not yet final. There had been no preliminary decision on March 12th. The court also rejected appellant's request that the doctrine of constructive filing be applied because an order dismissing one appeal could not be attacked by a separate appeal, because appellant was not incarcerated, and because the doctrine did not include orders terminating parental rights. The March 12th orders were not appealable because the statute provided only for review by extraordinary writ pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26(k), and appellant's request to treat the appeal as a writ petition was untimely because it was not made until after the § 366.26 hearing had been held.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal denying appellant mother's motion to deem the first notice of appeal to be a premature appeal from the orders made at the hearing of July 12, 1991, because there was not good cause for it to be an appeal from the orders made at the subsequent hearing. The court also rejected appellant's requests to allow the appeal under the theory of constructive filing or for treatment of the appeal as a writ petition.

COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX

DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Each side to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which denied appellant's constitutional challenge to respondent city's mobile home park rent stabilization ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner challenged the constitutionality of respondent city's mobile home park rent stabilization ordinance. Appellant argued that respondent's ordinance constituted a physical taking of its property. The court found respondent's ordinance on its face did validly regulate mobile home rent. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Manis


No. A049506


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO

October 14, 1992, Decided

DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which convicted appellant of a felony for willfully endangering the health of an elderly and dependent person under circumstances likely to produce great bodily harm or death in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 368(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant resided with her 79-year old mother who almost died from lack of food and water, and from infections left untreated. A jury convicted appellant of a felony for willfully endangering the health of an elderly and dependent person under circumstances likely to produce great bodily harm or death pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 368. Appellant challenged the conviction on several grounds. On appeal, the court only addressed the constitutionality of § 368. The court rejected appellant's argument that drew a distinction between § 368, and a child endangerment statute. The court rejected appellant's argument that § 368 violated due process rights of elderly persons who preferred in neglecting their medical needs. Polis v. City of La Palma


No. G012952


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


10 Cal. App. 4th 25; 12 Cal. Rptr. 2d 322; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1208; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8481; 92 Daily Journal DAR 13967



October 9, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Superior Court of Orange County, No. 692786, William F. Rylaarsdam, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed an order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which granted plaintiff city official's petition for a writ of mandate to compel the clerk for defendant to accept plaintiff's election nomination papers. Defendant contended that plaintiff was prohibited from running for office again by a city ordinance which limited city council members to two terms.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city official had served as a city council member for defendant city for two terms. Plaintiff presented nomination papers to the clerk of defendant in order to run for office for another term, which were refused due to a city ordinance that limited city council members to two terms. Plaintiff petitioned the trial court for a writ of mandate to compel defendant to accept his nomination papers. The trial court granted the motion and defendant appealed. The court affirmed the judgment and found that Cal. Gov't Code § 24001 set the eligibility requirements for local office. The court agreed with previous court decisions which found that legislature had intended to preempt local regulation of eligibility for election to local governing bodies. The court rejected defendant's argument that the statutes should have been construed to take into account changed conditions, because the issues involved whole statutory schemes that were not subject to the whims of public opinion. The court held that the statute did not grant power to defendant to change the qualifications of an elected official, and defendant had no special interest different from other cities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which granted plaintiff city official's petition for a writ of mandate to compel the clerk for defendant city to accept plaintiff's election nomination papers because state law had preempted the power of plaintiff to impose a term limitation on plaintiff's office through a city ordinance.

People v. Von Villas


No. B033751


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


10 Cal. App. 4th 201; 13 Cal. Rptr. 2d 62; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 1212; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8558; 92 Daily Journal DAR 14222



October 9, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for partial publication. All of the opinion is to be published with the exception of III (C).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A392422, Alexander H. Williams III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that convicted them for conspiracy to commit murder under Cal. Penal Code §§ 182 and 187 and robbery under Cal. Penal Code § 211 with a finding under Cal. Penal Code § 12022(a) of being armed with firearms. Defendants argued that the trial court improperly denied access to a writer's notes and tapes as protected under the journalist's shield law.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of conspiracy to commit murder and of robbery with firearms. On appeal they argued that they were improperly denied access to a writer's notes and tapes relative to a key witness, that secondary evidence of a lost item of evidence was improperly admitted and that juror misconduct required a new trial. The court affirmed, ruling that substantial evidence supported the finding that the writer's unpublished data was protected by the journalist's shield provision of Cal. Const. Art. I § 2(b) and Cal. Evid. Code § 1070 and the denial of access was not an abuse of discretion. The court also held that in the absence of bad faith on the part of the police, the failure to preserve potentially useful evidence did not constitute a denial of due process of law. The court further held that the trial court correctly denied the motion for new trial based upon allegations of jury misconduct because there was no showing that new evidence was improperly presented to the jury. The court also ruled that false imprisonment of the robbery victims was not an included offense of robbery and that the trial court properly excluded parts of transcripts of taped conversations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions, ruling that a writer's notes and tapes as to a key witness were protected under the journalist's shield law and the trial court's denial of access was not an abuse of discretion. The court also ruled that absent a showing of improper police motive, the loss of an item of evidence was not a denial of due process, and that there was no showing that new evidence was presented to the jury.
