In re Tania S.


No. D014258


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


5 Cal. App. 4th 728; 7 Cal. Rptr. 2d 60; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 508; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3312; 92 Daily Journal DAR 5126



April 16, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, Nos. J505373, J505374, J505375, J505376 and J505895, Michael J. Imhoff, Juvenile Court Referee.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review from the Superior Court of San Diego County, California, which made jurisdictional findings and a dispositional order in child dependency proceedings brought under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 300(a), 300(b) and 300(j). Appellant contended that the evidence did not support the findings and order and that the statute was unconstitutional. Respondent San Diego County Department of Social Services urged affirmance.


OVERVIEW: Respondent San Diego County Department of Social Services instigated dependency proceedings regarding appellant father's minor children. At the dispositional hearing the trial court declared the four oldest children at issue to be its dependent children. The court ordered removal of those children's custody from both parents under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 361(b)(1). The court ordered the children detained with their mother on specified conditions. Appellant father sought review. The reviewing court affirmed, finding that there was substantial evidence to support the conclusion that appellant was physically and emotionally abusive to his wife and their children. The juvenile court reasonably found that the children were at substantial risk of serious harm and that appellant's continued custody of them was not in their best interests. The appellate court exercised its discretion to consider a constitutional issue appellant raised for the first time on appeal. The court concluded that appellant lacked standing to pursue the issue. Appellant had not demonstrated that he suffered any direct injury resulting from the allegedly unconstitutional portion of the challenged statute.


OUTCOME: Jurisdictional findings and dispositional order in child dependency proceedings were affirmed. There was substantial evidence to support the finding that appellant father was physically and emotionally abusive to his children and that removal of appellant from the home was in the best interests of the children's well-being. Appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute at issue.

People v. Leung


No. H007885


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


5 Cal. App. 4th 482; 7 Cal. Rptr. 2d 290; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 478; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3139; 92 Daily Journal DAR 4933



April 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified April 28, 1992. Review Denied June 18, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 3176.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 140497, Jack Komar, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed. The abstracts of judgment are ordered modified by the trial court to reflect second degree robbery and attempted robbery convictions. The trial court is ordered to determine the number of days of custody credit to which David Leung is entitled and to amend David Leung's abstract of judgment to so reflect.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which convicted defendants of robbery, attempted robbery and false imprisonment and found weapons and arming enhancements true. Defendants challenged the prearrest photographic identification and the constitutionality of the restriction on voir dire in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code 223.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of robbery, attempted robbery and false imprisonment and the weapons and arming enhancements were found true. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, holding that the restriction on voir dire found in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code 223, did not violate U. S. Const. amend XIV, or Cal. Const. art. I, § 7, because the distinction between civil and criminal voir dire was rationally related to the legitimate state purpose of stopping abuse of the voir dire process. The court further held that the pre-arrest photographic identification of defendants was not suggestive because the photos presented for identification were of persons similar in age, complexion, and physical features. The court further held that the defendants' sentencing was proper because of the multiple acts of robbery and multiple victims. The court also ruled that the trial court could properly considered the defendants' lack of remorse when probation was denied.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were affirmed because the restrictions of voir dire in a criminal case did not violate the equal protection clause of the United States or California Constitutions. The court further held that the photographic lineup was not overly suggestive because the photos were of persons of similar age, complexion, and physical features.

People v. Hudson


No. B052294


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE.


5 Cal. App. 4th 131; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 690; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 469; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2973; 92 Daily Journal DAR 4657



April 6, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 23, 1992 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., Art VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 3759.
Kennard, J. and Arabian, J., are of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BA002571, J. D. Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), in which he was convicted of making terrorist threats in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 422. Defendant contended that § 422 was overbroad on its face in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I, and that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of making terrorist threats in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 422, when he told a coworker he was going to shoot a television journalist. On appeal, the court affirmed, and held that the fact that § 422 did not require an intent to carry out the threat did not affect its validity under U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that § 422 controlled pure speech and that the crime could be committed by words alone, without action or an intent to act. The court held that § 422 did not require that defendant have a specific intent that the threat be communicated to the intended victim, only that the statement be taken as a threat. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to conclude that defendant intended his threat to be taken seriously, including the nature of the threat, his previous obsessive behavior regarding the victim, his prior threat, and his possession of bullets. The victim's fear was sustained for a sufficient time to sustain the jury's finding. The facts surrounding the making of the threat were relevant and the trial court did not err in admitting the evidence. The prosecutor's comment regarding the rights of the jurors was not prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of making terrorist threats and held that the statute did not violate defendant's First Amendment rights because it was not overbroad. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict, and that the evidence was relevant and properly admitted.

MGW, Inc. v. Fredricks Dev. Corp.


No. G006654


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE.


12 Cal. App. 4th 244; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 888; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 463; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2886; 92 Daily Journal DAR 4491



April 2, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted July 9, 1992 (S015966), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 3500.
Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 5 Cal.App.4th 92.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 416196, Samuel B. Taylor, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed as it relates to the granting of Pacific Lighting's motions for new trial and for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and remanded to the trial court for the purpose of entering judgment for MGW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court vacated and remanded the order of the appellate court, which had reversed an order granting defendant development corporation a judgment notwithstanding the verdict and a new trial, affirmed an order of nonsuit for defendant financial corporations, and affirmed the award to plaintiff real estate broker of damages in plaintiff's action for interference with prospective economic advantage and conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff real estate broker filed suit when defendants, development and financial corporations, refused to pay a real estate commission as agreed. The court had reversed an order of the trial court, which granted defendant development corporation judgment notwithstanding the verdict and a new trial, affirmed orders of nonsuit for defendant financial corporations, and affirmed plaintiff's award of general and punitive damages. On remand, the court affirmed the award of damages and nonsuit and reversed the grant of a new trial and judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The court held that due process required that in an award of punitive damages, it was required to consider the reprehensibility of defendants' conduct, the deterrent effect in light of defendants' financial condition, and whether the punitive damages bore a reasonable relation to the actual damages. The court held that given the conspiratorial nature of defendants' conduct, the award was reasonable, that the ratio of punitive to actual damages fell within that approved in other California cases, and that there was sufficient financial data to determine that the awards would not cripple defendants' financial existence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order which granted defendant development corporation judgment notwithstanding the verdict and a new trial, affirmed the order of nonsuit in favor of defendant financial corporations, and affirmed the award to plaintiff real estate broker of damages based upon defendants' refusal to pay a commission. The court held that the trial court's method of reviewing damages did not violate defendants' due process rights.

Clark v. Kerby


No. A052837


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


4 Cal. App. 4th 1505; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 440; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 442; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2786; 92 Daily Journal DAR 4348



March 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 21, 1992. Review Denied April 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Humboldt County, No. DR 84237, J. Michael Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the judgment and remand: (a) for a determination of whether Clark was a known or reasonably ascertainable creditor of Copeland's estate, and (b) for further proceedings if necessary, consistent with Tulsa and this opinion. Costs on appeal to Clark.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Humboldt County (California), which barred appellant's claim against respondent, personal representative of decedent's estate, stemming from an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and decedent were involved in an automobile accident that apparently was the fault of decedent. Decedent died two months after the accident. Decedent's attorney commenced administration of the estate, and the court issued letters testamentary to respondent, decedent's daughter, as personal representative of the estate. Although appellant's attorney learned of decedent's death, appellant changed attorneys, and a creditor's claim against decedent's estate was not filed until 10 months later. Respondent rejected the claim, and appellant filed suit. The trial court ruled that appellant's claim was time-barred, and rejected appellant's motion for new trial. The court reversed, concluding that a recent United States Supreme Court opinion cast doubt on the validity of state nonclaim provisions. Due process rights required that a known or reasonably ascertainable creditor whose claim was not merely conjectural but who was not given actual notice of administration could not be cut off by a short claims filing period. The fact that appellant's attorney knew of decedent's death was not relevant; what was required was knowledge of administration, which appellant did not have.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment time-barring appellant's claim against respondent, personal representative of decedent's estate, was reversed. A known or reasonably ascertainable creditor with a non-conjectural claim was entitled to actual notice of an estate's administration. The court remanded the cause to determine whether appellant was a known or reasonably ascertainable creditor of decedent's estate and for further proceedings if necessary.

In re Jonathan B.


No. G010985


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


5 Cal. App. 4th 873; 7 Cal. Rptr. 2d 277; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 540; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3468; 92 Daily Journal DAR 5364



March 31, 1992, Decided

* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.

PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. J-423777, Richard G. Vogl, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) declaring her son a dependent of the juvenile court under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 300(b)-(c), (i).


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother challenged an order declaring her son a dependent of the juvenile court under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 300(b)-(c), (i). Appellant contended that § 300(c) was unconstitutionally vague and in violation of a number of guarantees of the United States and California Constitutions. She further argued that the trial court's order was unsupported by sufficient evidence as to any ground. The court affirmed, holding that in an appeal of a dependency proceeding finding, the fact that the juvenile court's finding under § 300(b) was supported by the evidence was sufficient to uphold the judgment of dependency. The court determined that the paramount underlying purpose of dependency proceedings was the protection of the child, and appellant did not represent a competing interest in that respect. The court concluded that the juvenile court exercised its broad discretion in determining that continued non-parental custody was in appellant's son's best interests and did not abuse that discretion.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed because in an appeal of a dependency proceeding finding, the fact that the juvenile court's finding was supported by the evidence was sufficient to uphold the judgment of dependency, and the juvenile court exercised its broad discretion in determining that continued non-parental custody was in appellant's son's best interests and did not abuse that discretion.

Consumers Union of U.S., Inc. v. Alta-Dena Certified Dairy


No. A046895


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


4 Cal. App. 4th 963; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 193; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 352; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2411; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3750

1163 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


City of Pomona v. Employers' Surplus Lines Ins. Co.


No. B032762


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE.


4 Cal. App. 4th 818; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 910; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 344; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2330; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3679; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3782



March 17, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 9, 1992 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 3519.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. EAC56699, Theodore D. Piatt and Thomas F. Nuss, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The summary judgments are reversed. The City of Pomona, G. Stanton Salby, Vernon M. Wiegand, E. J. Gaulding, Donna Smith, and Mark Nymeyer shall each recover their costs on appeal jointly and severally from Employers' Surplus Lines Insurance Company, Employer's Reinsurance Corporation, Pacific Indemnity Company, Harbor Insurance Company, and Twin City Fire Insurance Company.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insureds sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgments to five of respondent insurance companies for failing to defend appellants in connection with a third party civil rights action against one appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insureds sought review of a decision by the trial court, which granted summary judgments to five of respondent insurance companies for failing to defend appellant in connection with a third party civil rights action. The court reversed the trial court's judgments because respondents had failed to prove as a matter of law that the policy term "damages" unambiguously excluded coverage for the civil rights claims. The court held that resolution of the duty to defend depended upon whether coverage existed at the time the defense had to be commenced, not on whether respondents were ultimately required to pay monies to the third party plaintiff. Although the underlying complaint sought injunctive relief, respondents had a duty to defend because a suit for equitable relief could in some cases result in damages within the meaning of a general liability insurance policy and, in cases involving a complete violation of the right to vote, it was presumed a plaintiff was entitled to a damage award and costs and attorneys' fees could constitute damages within the meaning of the policies. The fact that the civil rights complaint did not seek damages did not preclude a duty to defend.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's summary judgments because respondent insurance companies had failed to prove as a matter of law that the term "damages" as used in their policies unambiguously excluded coverage for the claims in the civil rights action brought against appellant insured.

Walsh v. Board of Administration


No. C008704


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


4 Cal. App. 4th 682; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 118; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 319; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2246; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3514



March 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 6, 1992.
Review Denied June 11, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2926.
Mosk, J. is of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 361434, Joe S. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a former state legislator, challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Sacramento County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandate that sought to compel defendant board of administration of the public employees' retirement system to award him retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a former state legislator, appealed a judgment of the trial court which denied his petition for a writ of mandate. Appellant sought to compel defendant board of administration of the public employees' retirement system to award him retirement benefits, from the time he left legislative service in 1974 to the time he began drawing retirement benefits at age 60 in 1986, and to recalculate his current allowance based upon the cost of living increases that would have accrued during those years. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court because the court held that the modification of appellant's retirement benefits was consistent with the reservation of power to the legislature, and appellant failed to prove that the state was estopped to deny retirement benefits to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court because the court held that the modification of appellant's retirement benefits was consistent with the reservation of power to the legislature, and appellant failed to prove that the state was estopped to deny retirement benefits to him.

 

1165 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Pratali v. Gates


No. B058745


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.


4 Cal. App. 4th 632; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 733; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 326; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2298; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3558



March 13, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C700407, Philip M. Saeta, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Respondent to recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix sought review, on behalf of appellant decedent, of an order of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) that entered judgment in favor of respondent individual in his action on a prior judgment.


OVERVIEW: In 1967, appellant decedent executed a promissory note in another state, payable to respondent . When the note was not paid on the due date, respondent filed an action on the note. Almost ten years later, respondent received a judgment against appellant decedent. After entry of judgment, but prior to 1980, appellant decedent moved his domicile to another state. In 1987, respondent filed an application to renew the judgment, but his application was denied as untimely. Consequently, respondent filed a motion for relief from default. The motion was denied on the basis that the period for renewal of judgments ran after 10 years. In September 1988, respondent filed a separate action on the judgment of 1976. Appellant decedent died two months later, and appellant administratrix was substituted. The trial court entered judgment for respondent, and appellant moved for new trial. After the motion was denied, appellant sought review raising multiple points of error. On review, the court affirmed because the period of limitations was tolled up to the time respondent filed the separate action on the judgment, and the tolling did not violate any constitutional right of appellant decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of judgment, because the ten-year statute of limitations was tolled before appellant left the state and the period of limitations remained tolled up to the time of the filing of respondent individual's separate action on the original judgment, and such tolling did not violate appellant decedent's constitutional rights.

 

1166 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Claypool v. Wilson


No. C011580


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


4 Cal. App. 4th 646; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 77; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 314; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2221; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3443



March 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 13, 1992.
Review Denied June 18, 1992.
Mosk, J., and Kennard, J., were of the opinion that the petitions should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING: Application for a writ of mandate. Writ denied.



DISPOSITION: None of the claims of invalidity of Chapter 83 tendered by the Petitioners has merit. The alternative writ is discharged and the petition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, members of the Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS) and their employee organizations, sought a writ of mandamus (California) challenging the constitutionality of 1991 Cal. Stat. ch. 83, which repealed three funded supplemental cost of living programs, directed that the funds be used to offset contributions, and transferred the actuarial determinations from the PERS board to an actuary under a contract with respondent Governor.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, members of Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS) and employee organization, sought a writ of mandamus challenging the constitutionality of portions of 1991 Cal. Stat. ch. 83, which repealed supplemental cost of living programs, directed that funds be used to offset contributions due from PERS employers, and transferred the responsibility of actuarial determinations from the PERS board to an actuary acting under a contract with respondent Governor. Petitioners contended that the repeal of the supplemental programs and the reallocation of the funds unconstitutionally impaired the contract rights of PERS beneficiaries and, along with the transfer of actuarial functions, violated Cal. Const. art. XVI, § 17, which declared that the assets of a public pension or retirement system were trust funds. The court denied the petition and held that the statute did not impair previously existing contract rights because petitioners who had earned vested contract rights by rendering service under the repealed statutes were given comparable advantages under the new supplemental program, and that previous employees had no vested rights that could have been impaired.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioners', members of the Public Employees' Retirement System and employee organizations, petitioner for mandamus and held that a law which repealed various supplemental cost of living programs and redirected funding from them was consistent with trust law and did not violate petitioners' preexisting contractual rights. The court held that the law was constitutional.

 

1167 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Batiste v. Superior Court


No. B062594


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE.


4 Cal. App. 4th 460; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 694; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 307; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2083



March 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 27, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2825.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BS010989, Ronald E. Swearinger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition is denied. The alternative writ of mandate issued on November 25, 1991, is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandate directing respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County to vacate its order that denied petitioner's application for a writ of mandate ordering the municipal court to sustain his demurrer to a charge that petitioner violated a municipal code that prohibited entering a fenced area of the city airport. Petitioner contended that state law had preempted this area and that the ordinance was vague.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a fenced area at the city airport, which was posted with no trespassing signs. He was subsequently charged with violation of a city ordinance which prohibited such conduct. Petitioner filed a demurrer to the charge, which was rejected by the municipal court. Petitioner requested a writ of mandate from the trial court, seeking an order directing the municipal court to sustain his demurrer. The trial court denied the writ, and petitioner then sought a writ of mandate from the court directing the trial court to vacate and set aside its order. Petitioner contended that the municipal code was preempted by state law, and was unconstitutionally vague. The court denied petitioner's writ, and held that state law had not preempted the area because the municipal code dealt with access to any fenced and posted area of the airport while that state law dealt only with areas of airport operations. Therefore the laws did not conflict and the subject matter of airport access was not fully and completely covered by state law. The court also held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because a reasonable person did not have to guess at its meaning.


OUTCOME: The court denied a petition for writ of mandate that sought to direct the trial court to vacate its order denying petitioner's application for a writ of mandate to order the municipal court to sustain petitioner's demurrer to a charge that he violated a municipal code prohibiting entry into a fenced area at the airport. The code pertained to an area not covered by state law and therefore there was no conflict and no state preemption.

Salinas Union High School Dist. v. Honig


No. H008187


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


4 Cal. App. 4th 357; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 626; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 279; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2007; 92 Daily Journal DAR 3066



March 6, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 21, 1992 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art VI, § 14, rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2576.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Monterey County, No. 90956, Robert A. O'Farrell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter remanded for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants school districts challenged the decision from the Superior Court of Monterey County (California) which denied appellants' writ of mandate seeking to require appellee state to reimburse appellants for expenses incurred in reliance upon appellee's promise to reimburse school districts who provide behind-the-wheel driver's training to students.


OVERVIEW: Appellants school districts attempted to enforce a promise made by appellee state promising to reimburse appellants for expenses incurred for providing behind-the-wheel driver's training to eligible students. The state had paid for 37 years prior and appellants argued that, once they had provided the services, they had a vested right in the reimbursement. The trial court denied the writ of mandate and appellants challenged the denial. The court held that, while appellants were entitled to reimbursement based on the vested right, the payment could not be ordered from the Driver Training Penalty Assessment Fund because the money therein had not been continuously appropriated as required. However, the court also found that appellants could seek reimbursement from another source of money and therefore they reversed the denial of the writs, granting them, and remanded for further proceedings awarding costs to appellants.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellants' petitions for writs of mandate seeking to require appellee state to reimburse them for expenses incurred in driver's training instruction was reversed and remanded for further proceedings because appellants had a vested right to the reimbursement and appellee was equitably estopped from denying the payment from whatever monies were available.

Horsemen's Benevolent & Protective Assn. v. Valley Racing Assn.


No. F013671


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


4 Cal. App. 4th 1538; 6 Cal. Rptr. 2d 698; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 464; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3028; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3029; 92 Daily Journal DAR 4742; 92 Daily Journal DAR 4783



March 6, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication. Those portions directed to be published follow.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified Aprril 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 370132-3, Stephen R. Henry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed and the cause remanded with direction to the trial court to determine reasonable attorney fees for services performed on appeal and add such fee to the principal amount of the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant racing association challenged the decision from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California) which found that it had breached the written purse agreement with appellee horsemen's association and awarded appellee damages with interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellee horsemen's association filed a complaint for damages arising from breach of a written purse agreement that appellant racing association violated by unilaterally reducing the purse. After the jury found for appellee horsemen's association appellant challenged the ruling arguing that appellant did not have standing, that appellant did not exhaust its administrative remedies, the trial court failed to interpret statutory terms correctly, and that its actions were excused by administrative action. The court first held that the standing issue did not apply to the situation. The court further held that there was no specific language or legislative intent granting the California Horse Racing Board the authority to award damages in these types of disputes. In addition the court held that appellee was estopped from bringing the interpretation issues. The court also held that appellant's actions were not excused by statute or regulation. The court therefore affirmed the judgment and remanded for a determination of reasonable attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding appellee racing association liable for breach of a written purse agreement was affirmed because appellee's actions were not excused by any action taken by the California Horse Racing Board (Board), nor did the Board have the authority to award damages in this type of dispute.

 

1170 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Daniels v. McMahon


No. A052355


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


4 Cal. App. 4th 48; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 404; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 590; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1835; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2813



March 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 147054, Demetrios P. Agretelis and Dawn B. Girard, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant benefit recipient sought review of an order by a Superior Court of Alameda County (California) which dismissed its action against respondent director, by which appellant sought to invalidate respondent's policy of considering "aid paid pending" in its calculation of net available income in order to determine appellant's eligibility for supplemental income pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 11450.2.


OVERVIEW: Appellant benefit recipient filed a complaint for injunctive and declaratory relief and a petition for writ of mandate. Appellant challenged respondent director's policy to include "aid paid pending" the outcome of hearings on reduced Aid to Families with Dependent Children payments in its calculation of net available income when determining eligibility for supplemental payments pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 11450.2. Appellant received "aid paid pending" in the amount of appellant's maximum aid payment, but was denied supplemental income. It was determined that appellant had received an overpayment and had to repay the "aid paid pending." Appellant argued that respondent's policy violated the purpose of § 11450.2 and violated equal protection and due process. The court held that respondent's policy did not violate the statute's purpose because appellant never had to live on less than 80 percent of the maximum aid payment. The court held that there was an obvious correspondence between the classification and the goal of the statute because the system was rationally calculated to achieve its goal of assisting families most in need of immediate cash.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the action. Respondent director's policy to include "aid paid pending" as net available income when determining supplementary benefits eligibility did not violate the purpose of the welfare statute because appellant benefit recipient never received less than 80 percent of his maximum aid payment. The policy was rationally calculated to achieve the statutory goal of assisting families most in need of immediate cash.

 

1171 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Howitt v. Superior Court


No. D013700


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


3 Cal. App. 4th 1575; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 196; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 240; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1844; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2764



February 28, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Imperial County, No. 70412, Henry Wien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied without prejudice to a renewal of the petition in the superior court and further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By a petition for extraordinary relief, petitioner sheriff argued that respondent, the Superior Court of Imperial County (California), erred in denying his request that the county counsel's office disqualify itself from acting as adviser to the employment appeals board while acting as advocate for a party before it.


OVERVIEW: A dispute between petitioner sheriff and a county sheriff's department was scheduled for an administrative hearing before the county employment appeals board. Upon learning that the county counsel's office would be advising that board and writing its decision while also acting as advocate for the county sheriff's department, petitioner sought disqualification of the county counsel's office. He brought this petition for extraordinary relief upon respondent superior court's denial of his request. The court held that in combining advocacy and decisionmaking roles, county counsel had the burden to show that adequate screening procedures existed for due process purposes and that the lawyer advising the board had no potential involvement in the case. The petition for writ of mandate was denied without prejudice to a renewal of the petition in the superior court.


OUTCOME: As the county counsel's office combined advocacy and decisionmaking roles, the court held that it had the burden to show adequate screening procedures for due process purposes. The petition for writ of mandate was denied without prejudice to a renewal of the petition in the superior court.

 

1172 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Jeremy W.


No. D013997


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


3 Cal. App. 4th 1407; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 148; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 221; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2600



February 26, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. J500757, Hideo Chino, Referee.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. The matter is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought relief from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), terminating her parental rights to her minor son pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26. The judgment was entered after the court summarily denied appellant's petition pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 388 requesting that the hearing date be modified or set aside.


OVERVIEW: The minor child of appellant mother was removed from her custody and a reunification plan was established. At a 12-month review hearing, the juvenile court referee terminated reunification services and ordered a Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26 hearing to determine the child's adoptability and terminate appellant's parental rights. Prior to the § 366.26 hearing, appellant petitioned under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 388, requesting that the order setting the § 366.26 hearing date be modified or set aside. The juvenile court denied the petition summarily without a hearing and cited no factual reasons for its conclusion that the child's best interests would not be promoted by a change in the order. On appeal, the court held that once appellant made a prima facie showing of a favorable change in her circumstances including almost full compliance with the court ordered reunification plan, procedural due process required that appellant be granted a full and fair § 388 hearing on the merits. After reviewing the record, the court concluded that the juvenile court's summary denial of appellant's petition without a hearing was not support by the record and thus was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Order denying appellant mother's petition for a hearing to set aside the juvenile court's order terminating reunification services was reversed and the cause was remanded to juvenile court with instructions to schedule a hearing to determine appellant's parental stability as it related to her fulfillment of the goals established by the reunification plan.

Cottle v. Superior Court


No. B060125


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


3 Cal. App. 4th 1367; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 882; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 237; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2612



February 26, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, Nos. 95460 and 99933, Melinda A. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ is discharged, the stay issued herein on August 1, 1991, is vacated, and the petition for a writ of mandate is denied. The July 2, 1991, order of the court excluding petitioners from introducing evidence that their physical injuries were caused by exposure to hazardous material or toxic waste at the Dunes is affirmed as expressed in the views in this opinion. Real parties in interest to recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, alleged toxic tort victims, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County(California), which precluded petitioners from submitting evidence at trial that their personal physical injuries were caused by exposure to toxic chemicals.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, alleged toxic tort victims, sought review of an order which excluded petitioners from submitting evidence at trial that their personal physical injuries were caused by exposure to toxic chemicals. The court affirmed the order of the trial court precluding petitioners from introducing evidence that their physical injuries were caused by exposure to hazardous material or toxic waste. The trial court, as part of its trial management program, had asked petitioners to establish a prima facie case, on the eve of trial, that the personal injuries were caused by hazardous material or toxic waste. When petitioners were unable to do so, the trial court prohibited petitioners from introducing evidence on that claim at trial. The court found that under the Trial Court Delay Reduction Act, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 68600 et seq., the trial court had managed its delay reduction program in a manner which was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court excluding petitioners, alleged toxic tort victims, from introducing evidence that their physical injuries were caused by exposure to hazardous material or toxic waste, because they failed to allege a prima facie claim for personal injury.

People v. Banner


No. F014642, No. F015946


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


3 Cal. App. 4th 1315; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 125; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 216; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2663



February 25, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I.C., I.D., I.E., I.F., I.G., I.H., II, III, IV, V, and the "Facts."


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied April 29, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2286.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 42288A, Gary T. Friedman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Insofar as the petition requests relief from this court in addition to that granted above, said request is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which convicted and sentenced him for second degree robbery, being under the influence of a controlled substance, and possession of narcotics paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was found guilty of the charged crimes, the trial court denied appellant's application for probation and imposed an aggravated sentence, including enhancements for appellant's prior convictions. Appellant argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel requiring a reversal of the judgment of conviction. On appeal, the court examined Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 223 (Proposition 115). The court found defense counsel accepted the jury without exercising any peremptory challenges. Appellant contended that his counsel's performance during jury selection deprived him of the effective assistance of counsel at a critical stage of the proceedings. The court held appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutional validity of Proposition 115. The court determined that appellant failed to establish that he was adversely impacted by the procedure and he has failed to establish the trial court's voir dire of the jury was deficient. The court held that the limitation of voir dire to determine challenges for cause under Proposition 115 did not violate appellant's rights. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing appellant for multiple offenses was affirmed, because appellant did not have standing to challenge a law related to the voir dire of the jury.

City of Los Altos v. Barnes


No. H008251


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


3 Cal. App. 4th 1193; 5 Cal. Rptr. 2d 77; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 211; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1562; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2404



February 24, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 14, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2471.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. P53399, Taketsugu Takei and William F. Brown, Jr., Judges.



DISPOSITION: In sum, we conclude that the challenged ordinance is constitutional and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in issuing the preliminary injunction. The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which granted respondent municipality's preliminary injunction prohibiting appellant from carrying on a home occupation at her residence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowner owned and operated a recreational family camp. She completed certain camp-related tasks at her residence. Respondent municipality filed a lawsuit against appellant to enjoin her from violating a zoning ordinance. The trial court issued a preliminary injunction. Appellant contended that the trial court did not apply the correct test in determining whether to grant the injunction. The court found that appellant did not request a statement of the trial court's decision and that the trial court was not obligated to provide one for a preliminary injunction because it was not the equivalent of a trial. Appellant conceded that she violated the ordinance by paying individuals to perform camp-related tasks at her residence. Thus, there was a rebuttable presumption that the potential harm to the public outweighed any harm to appellant. The zoning ordinance was constitutional, because appellant's rights to privacy were not violated. Additionally, the ordinance was not vague, because a person of reasonable intelligence would know that appellant's conduct was prohibited. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that granted respondent's a preliminary injunction against appellant was affirmed, because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the injunction and the zoning ordinance that prohibited appellant's conduct was constitutional.

Evans v. City of San Jose


No. H008169


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


3 Cal. App. 4th 728; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 601; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 156; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1333; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2145



February 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 29, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2292.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 697780, Peter G. Stone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons and not because Evans failed to exhaust her administrative remedies, the judgment is affirmed. Costs on appeal to respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review from a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city in an action brought by plaintiff challenging the facial constitutionality of Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 36500 et seq. and San Jose, Cal. Ordinance No. 22960.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged the facial constitutionality of Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 36500 et seq. (Act) and San Jose, Cal. Ordinance No. 22960 (ordinance), which authorized imposition of assessments on businesses for the purpose of general downtown promotion, the furnishing of music, and other expenditures unrelated to capital improvements. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city. On appeal, the court concluded that plaintiff satisfied her obligations to pursue administrative remedies. Plaintiff filed and pursued her protest to the formation of the business improvement district (BID) before the city council; she sent in her ballot formally registering a protest and a separate letter further explaining her objections to the proposed BID. However, the court disagreed with plaintiff that the Act and ordinance imposed a "special tax" without requiring a concurring vote of two-thirds of the electorate and, therefore, violated Cal. Const. art. XIII A. The court held that the assessment was not a "special tax" as contemplated by Cal. Const. art. XIII A. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city. The assessment on businesses for the purpose of general downtown promotion was not a "special tax" as contemplated by the California Constitution.

 

1177 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Greene v. Amante


No. G010762


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


3 Cal. App. 4th 684; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 571; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 162; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1275; 92 Daily Journal DAR 2020



February 11, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 568445, Jack K. Mandel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons stated in the unpublished portion of this opinion, the order awarding sanctions is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which imposed discovery sanctions on him in an amount greater than $ 750.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney sought relief from the trial court's order imposing sanctions on him in the amount of $ 794 for his failure to fully respond to interrogatories. The issue was whether appellant could appeal the order as of right prior to entry of final judgment in the underlying litigation. The court held that he could, and then affirmed the order imposing sanctions. The court grounded its holding regarding the timing of the appeal on Cal. Civ. Proc. § 904.1(k). The court reviewed the legislative history of this statute and concluded that the legislature intended to create a "bright line" at $ 750, above which immediate appellate scrutiny of a sanctions order was authorized. The court held that the legislature intended to strike a balance between judicial administration and the right to immediate review of a sanctions order, which in some cases might cripple an attorney's practice. The court also held that the effect of § 904.1(k) was to allow an appeal from any sanctions order provided the amount in controversy exceeded $ 750.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order imposing discovery sanctions on appellant attorney in an amount greater than $ 750 because a sanctions order exceeding $ 750 was immediately appealable despite the fact that a final judgment had not been entered in the underlying litigation. There was nothing in the record to indicate that the order was not justified.

In re Jennifer S.


No. F015507


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


3 Cal. App. 4th 568; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 541; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 150; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1206; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1940



February 7, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied April 16, 1992 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 1820.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kings County, No. 8506, Louis F. Bissig, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the juvenile court terminating appellant's parental rights is reversed and the matter is remanded for a new assessment and hearing of the suitability of the prospective adoptive parents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kings County (California), which sustained the petition filed by respondent department of human services declaring that appellant's dependent children be placed with foster parents and terminating the parental rights of appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother challenged a judgment that declared that appellant's dependent children be placed with foster parents. Respondent department of human services requested that appellant's parental rights be terminated and that the older child be placed with the father and the drug-addicted infant with foster parents. Appellant claimed the social worker's report inadequately addressed the issue of suitability of the adoptive parents. The requirement of an assessment of prospective adoptive families was intended to protect the individual rights of the minors and the natural parents. The court held that the record did not establish any actual or substantial compliance with Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.21(i)(4) and a proper assessment must be completed. Appellant claimed that insufficient evidence was presented to support a finding that the infant was adoptable. The evidence in the report supported the finding that the minor was adoptable without respect to the suitability of her foster parents. The order of the juvenile court terminating appellant's parental rights was reversed and the matter remanded for a new assessment of the prospective adoptive parents.


OUTCOME: The order of the juvenile court terminating appellant mother's parental rights was reversed and the matter remanded for a new assessment of the suitability of the prospective adoptive parents, which was initiated by a petition filed by respondent Department of Human Services, on the termination of the parental rights of appellant. The court held that the infant was adoptable without respect to the suitability of her foster parents.

 

1179 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Thornton


No. E007941


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


3 Cal. App. 4th 419; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 519; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 135; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1107; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1759



February 4, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * ]


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts B, C, and D.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Inyo County, No. 16595, Donald L. Chapman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed as to both defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Inyo County (California), which convicted him of robbery. The trial court allowed state to impeach defendant on the basis of his prior conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 422, for making terroristic threats.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's robbery conviction. The court held that defendant's prior conviction for violating Cal. Penal Code § 422, was properly used to impeach him because § 422 was a crime of moral turpitude and it could be said with substantial assurance that defendant's credibility was adversely affected by his having suffered the conviction. The court looked to the statutory definition of the crime to determine whether the least adjudicated elements of the conviction necessarily showed any character trait that could reasonably be characterized as "immoral." The court rejected defendant's argument that § 422, like battery, Cal. Penal Code § 243, was not a crime of moral turpitude because it did not require an intent to carry out the threatened injury. The court found that § 422 punished a knowing infliction of mental terror that deserved moral condemnation. The court held that the making of threats described in § 422 violated generally accepted standards of moral behavior, whether or not defendant intended to carry out those threats.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's robbery conviction because the trial court properly allowed the state to impeach defendant with evidence of his prior conviction for making terroristic threats. The making of terroristic threats was a crime of moral turpitude because the knowing infliction of mental terror deserved moral condemnation.

 

1180 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Greenpeace, USA v. City of Glendale


No. B050559


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO.


3 Cal. App. 4th 340; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 672; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 118; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1055; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1665



February 3, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C619206, William W. Huss, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The matter is remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion. Each side shall bear their respective costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, environmental activists and individual, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent City of Glendale in appellants' action for declaratory and injunctive relief against enforcement of ordinances that regulated charitable solicitation, which appellants claimed violated their equal protection and freedom of speech rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, environmental activists and individual, sought declaratory and injunctive relief against the enforcement by respondent City of Glendale of two ordinances which regulated charitable solicitations, one that required solicitors to submit to fingerprinting, and the other that exempted those organizations which had maintained headquarters in the city for three years. Appellants alleged that the ordinances violated their federal and state constitutional rights to freedom of speech and equal protection. Both parties filed cross motions for summary judgment. The trial court issued an order that granted respondent's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded since both ordinances were unconstitutional. The court held that although respondent had a compelling interest to deter fraud, the fingerprint ordinance was not narrowly tailored, it chilled freedom of speech, and less restrictive means were available. The court ruled that the second ordinance's durational residence requirement violated equal protection in that it was not narrowly tailored, and it was not necessary to promote respondent's interest in fraud deterrence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent City of Glendale and remanded since the ordinances that regulated appellants', environmental activists and individual, charitable solicitations were unconstitutional. The ordinances were not narrowly tailored, and less restrictive means were available to accomplish respondent's purpose of fraud deterrence.

Garrick Development Co. v. Hayward Unified School Dist.


No. A051182


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


3 Cal. App. 4th 320; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 897; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 127; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1048; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1676



February 3, 1992, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication except for the discussion under the heading "Equal educational opportunity" in part IV.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 2, 1992.
Review Denied April 23, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, Nos. H-136556-2, H-137824-1 and H-138447-9, Joanne C. Parrilli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which denied appellants' petitions for writ of mandate in a consolidated case against appellees school district and board to recover fees appellants paid under Cal. Gov. Code §§ 53080, 65995.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developers challenged the trial court's denial of their petition for writ of mandate by which appellants sought to recover fees paid to appellees school district and board under Cal. Gov. Code §§ 53080, 65995. Appellants asserted that the fees were in violation of statutory requirements and constitutional limitations. The court affirmed the lower court's order and found that the fees were not a special tax which would required a two-thirds voter approval under Cal. Const. art. XIII A § 4 because the fees were not levied as general revenue but for a specific need and did not exceed the reasonable cost of facilities provided by appellees. Cal. Gov. Code §§ 53080, 65995 created fees that were not arbitrary, unreasonable, and had a substantial relation to the public welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court which denied appellants' petitions for writ of mandate because the resolutions that created the fees appellants sought to recover did not exceed constitutional limits and did not violate state statutes.

 

1182 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Jennilee T.


Nos. G010662, G010957


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


3 Cal. App. 4th 212; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 101; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 116; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1004; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1553



January 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 27, 1992.
Review Denied May 14, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2466.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. J-422838, Robert J. Polis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which found that they were gravely mentally disabled under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 361.5(b)(2), and thus incapable of utilizing reunification services mandated by Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 361.5(a). Appellants also challenged the trial court's finding under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26, that their daughter was adoptable.


OVERVIEW: When appellant parents, both institutionalized for mental illness, had a baby, it was placed with respondent social services. At a dispositional hearing, the trial court declared the minor a dependent of the court and found that under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 361.5(b)(2), reunification services were not required. After a hearing under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26, the trial court found that the minor could not be returned to appellants and it was likely that she would be adopted. On appeal, the court held that Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 361.5(c), was not unconstitutional because it created a permissible legislative classification. It was reasonable for the state to distinguish between those who could and could not benefit from reunification services under § 361.5(c). Further, § 361.5(c), did not deprive appellants of due process where expert testimony showed that they were incapable of utilizing reunification services. The court held there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's finding that the minor would be adopted in the foreseeable future under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26(c)(1), where a relative and four other families expressed interest in adopting her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which found appellant parents incapable of utilizing reunification services and that their daughter was adoptable. The statutory provision permitting the trial court to find that reunification services were not required under certain circumstances was constitutional. Sufficient evidence showed that the daughter was adoptable based on testimony that four families and a great aunt had shown interest.

George v. International Soc'y for Krishna Consciousness


'No. D007153


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE.


3 Cal. App. 4th 52; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 473; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 105; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 985; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1593



January 30, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 2, 1992. Review Denied April 29, 1992 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 2267.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 277565, James A. Jackman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed insofar as it awards damages to Robin George for false imprisonment, intentional infliction of emotional distress and libel with instructions to the trial court to enter judgment in favor of defendants as to those causes of action. Insofar as it awards punitive damages to Marcia George, the judgment is also reversed. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed. As between Robin George and defendants, the parties are to bear their respective costs for this appeal. Marcia George shall recover all her costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Supreme Court, the court reconsidered its decision to uphold a punitive damages award against defendant Krishna Consciousness, where the damages were imposed without consideration of defendant's financial condition, in a suit brought by appellants, mother and daughter, arising from the alleged brainwashing of appellant daughter by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, mother and daughter, brought an action against defendant Krishna Consciousness for false imprisonment, intentional infliction of emotional distress, wrongful death of plaintiffs' husband and father, and libel. The trial jury awarded plaintiffs compensatory and punitive damages. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment as to all of plaintiff daughter's claims except her wrongful death claim and denied all of defendant's claims. Both parties appealed to the United States Supreme Court, which remanded the case back to the court for reconsideration. Upon reconsideration, the court reaffirmed its original decision as to daughter's claims, but reversed itself as to defendant's damage claims and remanded the case to the trial court for retrial on plaintiff mother's punitive damage award. The court found that new legal precedent had been issued since the commencement of plaintiffs' action that applied retroactively to plaintiff mother's punitive damages claim. Plaintiff mother was required mother to present evidence of defendant's financial condition so that a jury could award damages that would punish and deter defendant's behavior without destroying it financially.


OUTCOME: The court reaffirmed its decision denying plaintiff daughter's compensatory and punitive damages, but reversed its decision as to defendant Krishna Consciousness' punitive damages claim, and remanded the case for limited retrial on the issue of mother's punitive damages, because evidence of defendant's financial condition was necessary to support an award of punitive damages, and plaintiff mother had the burden of producing such evidence.

 

1184 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Donaldson v. Lungren


No. B055657


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX.


2 Cal. App. 4th 1614; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 59; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 104; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 880; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1439



January 29, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Barbara County, No. 181830, Ronald C. Stevens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The parties to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, patient and cryogenic suspension participant, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which dismissed their action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, attorney general, district attorney, and coroner. Plaintiffs asserted that plaintiff patient had a constitutional right to premortem cryogenic suspension of his body.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, patient and cryogenic suspension participant, sought a declaration that plaintiff patient had a constitutional right to premortem cryogenic suspension of his body and the assistance of others in achieving that state. Plaintiffs sought an injunction against criminal prosecution of participants in the procedure and against the coroner performing an autopsy on the body after death. The trial court sustained a demurrer brought by defendants, attorney general, district attorney, and coroner. On appeal, the court held that there was no constitutional right to assisted suicide and that the trial court could not enjoin public officers from performing official acts that they were required to do by law. The act of taking one's own life with the assistance of others was not the exercise of the right to refuse medical treatment. Allowing another individual to take aid plaintiff patient's suicide violated Cal. Penal Code § 401, even though suicide itself was not illegal. The court held that § 401, did not violate plaintiff cryogenic suspension participant's constitutional right to free speech. There was no constitutional protection for a planned participation in another's suicide.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which sustained a demurrer brought by defendants, attorney general, district attorney, and coroner, in an action brought by plaintiffs, patient and cryogenic suspension participant, concerning the constitutional right to premortem cryogenic suspension. There was no constitutional right to an assisted suicide, and the act of assisting or encouraging another's suicide was a felony.

People v. Diaz


No. D013341


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


18 Cal. App. 4th 1647; 3 Cal. Rptr. 2d 658; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 62; 92 Daily Journal DAR 947



January 21, 1992, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted April 16, 1992 (S025443), Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 1789.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 2 Cal. App. 4th 1275 and 8 Cal. App. 4th 1448 and 13 Cal. App. 4th 1315.)] October 21, 1993 Review Transferred to Court of Appeal, Fourth Appellate District Division One with directions to vacate and reconsider, Reported at: 1993 Cal LEXIS 5580. (See 20 Cal. App. 4th 1257.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR116825, Charles L. Patrick, Judge. * 


* Judge of the Municipal Court for the San Diego Judicial District sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of burglary and challenged that portion of the judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which ordered restitution under Cal. Gov't. Code § 13967(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary and challenged that portion of the judgment that ordered restitution, taken from his prison wages pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2085.5, for loss of a jacket and transmission damage, contending that the order was invalid and unconstitutional. The court struck that portion of the judgment to take restitution from prison wages and affirmed the remainder. The court held that to impose restitution under Cal. Gov't. Code § 13967(c), the economic loss suffered by the victim must have resulted from appellant's criminal conduct. The court held under the "plain meaning" rule and legislative history that "result" was defined as any injury done to any person resulting from a breach of the law, for all damages actually caused by the crime. The court held that the problems with the transmission were triggered by victim's reaction to appellant's unlawful presence at her house and thus the damage was a result of appellant's criminal conduct since the damage was actually caused by and a logical consequence of such conduct. Thus, as the damage to the car arose from such conduct; the economic loss that arose out of such damage falls within the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that ordered restitution and struck that portion to take restitution from prison wages. The court held that the problems with the transmission were triggered by victim's reaction to appellant's unlawful presence at her house and thus the economic loss arose out of the criminal conduct.

People v. Jones


No. B046297


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE.


2 Cal. App. 4th 867; 3 Cal. Rptr. 2d 602; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 55; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 540; 92 Daily Journal DAR 739



January 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 26, 1992, Reported at 1992 Cal. LEXIS 1520.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A578629, Melvin B. Grover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is directed to prepare a corrected abstract of judgment reflecting "actual local time" of 285 days. As so modified the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of second-degree robbery pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 211.


OVERVIEW: Appellant presented no defense when he represented himself at trial and was convicted of second degree robbery, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 211. Appellant sought review of the conviction, and the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, with a modification. The court held that the trial court did not err when it failed to instruct appellant sua sponte on the lesser included offense of grand theft from the person because there was no contradictory evidence concerning the circumstances of the robbery. The use of force was compelling because the victim suffered an injury, though minor, and appellant presented no defense. The court held that the trial court did not have a duty to advise appellant that he had a right to testify because the general rule was that a self-represented person was not entitled to any assistance or advice from the trial judge on matters of law, evidence, or trial practice. The court directed the trial court to correct the abstract of judgment to reflect the actual local time of 285 days.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, as modified, the decision of the trial court, which convicted appellant of second-degree robbery because appellant presented no contradictory evidence that would have allowed an instruction on the lesser included offense of grand theft and because the trial court did not have a duty to advise self-represented appellant that he had a right to testify.

In re Marriage of Colvin


No. A049096


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


2 Cal. App. 4th 1570; 4 Cal. Rptr. 2d 323; 1992 Cal. App. LEXIS 128; 92 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1089; 92 Daily Journal DAR 1745



January 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Ordered Published February 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 738195, Carlos P. Baker, Jr., Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Municipal Court for the Corcoran Judicial District sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which refused to allocate the community interest in his pension plan according to the method set forth in recent amendments to the Judges' Retirement Law and instead applied Cal. Civ. Code § 4800.8 (1988) in a post-divorce pension allocation action.


OVERVIEW: When appellant ex-husband and respondent ex-wife divorced, appellant asked that the court retain jurisdiction over his retirement plan and to distribute pension benefits at maturity. Subsequently, appellant's retirement plan placed a hold on his account pending a determination of the parties' community interests. The trial court refused to allocate the community interest in appellant's pension plan according to the method set forth in recent Judges' Retirement Law (JRL) amendments and instead applied Cal. Civ. Code § 4800.8 (1988), which was more favorable to respondent. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly exercised its discretion, because § 4800.8 applied retroactively. The court noted that the divorce reservation clause was not open-ended and that the trial court only retained limited supervisory authority over the retirement plan. The court also concluded that § 4800.8 and the JRL amendments were discretionary and that the retirement plan's interpretation was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the retroactive application of the retirement plan statute, holding that the trial court only retained limited supervisory authority over appellant ex-husband's retirement plan, despite his request for the trial court to retain jurisdiction and that application of a statute instead of the Judicial Retirement Law amendments was discretionary.
